==================== START: act-phase-completion-checklist ====================
# ACT Phase Completion Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that the ACT phase (Strategic Advisor + Strategic Innovator) has completed all essential work to transition from strategic planning to operational execution. This checklist ensures the strategic decision has been translated into a detailed, actionable, innovation-enriched implementation plan that guides organizational execution.

## What This Phase Accomplishes

The ACT phase operationalizes strategy. The Strategic Advisor and Innovator together ensure:
- Strategy is translated into executable plan
- Innovation opportunities are integrated
- Accountability and ownership are clear
- Resources are allocated and sequenced
- Success metrics are defined
- Organization is ready to execute

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. Execution Plan Detailed & Sequenced ‚úì

- [ ] **Plan is broken into executable phases**
  - Quick wins/proof points (0-3 months)
  - Phase 1: Foundation building (0-6 months)
  - Phase 2: Scale/implementation (6-12 months)
  - Phase 3: Optimization/learning (12-24 months)
  - Clear milestones and gates between phases

- [ ] **Within each phase, activities are specific**
  - What specifically needs to happen? (Clear actions, not abstractions)
  - In what sequence? (Dependencies clear)
  - By when? (Dates or relative timing)
  - Who is responsible? (Owner assigned)
  - What's the success condition? (How do we know it's done?)

- [ ] **Critical path is identified**
  - What activities must happen first?
  - What activities are dependent on others?
  - Which activities are longest lead time?
  - What's the critical path to success?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
PHASE 1: FOUNDATION (Months 0-6)

Activity 1.1: Organizational Structure
- Create SMB Product Team (Product lead, 3 engineers, 1 designer)
- Create SMB GTM Team (Sales leader, 3 AEs, 1 marketing specialist)
- Establish governance (weekly steering committee)
- Timeline: Weeks 1-4 | Owner: VP Products | Success: Teams in place, charter defined

Activity 1.2: Product Requirements Definition
- Document simplified feature set for SMB
- Prioritize MVP features for launch
- Plan roadmap for years 1-3
- Timeline: Weeks 2-8 | Owner: SMB Product Lead | Success: PRD approved

Activity 1.3: Go-to-Market Strategy
- Define SMB positioning vs. enterprise
- Plan sales model (direct, partnerships, self-serve tiers)
- Create messaging framework
- Timeline: Weeks 3-8 | Owner: SMB Sales Lead | Success: GTM plan approved

Activity 1.4: Build Partnerships
- Identify potential channel partners
- Negotiate partnership terms
- Recruit partners for launch
- Timeline: Weeks 4-26 | Owner: SMB Sales Lead | Success: 3-5 partnerships signed

CRITICAL PATH:
- Hiring (slow; limit other timelines) ‚Üí Start Week 1
- Product requirements (blocks development) ‚Üí Complete by Week 8
- Partner identification (long sales cycles) ‚Üí Start Week 4

PHASE GATE: By end of Month 6, have teams in place, product plan set, partnerships identified
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Gantt chart level detail
- ‚ùå Every task specified
- ‚ùå Complete resource specifications
- ‚ùå Detailed budget breakdown

---

### 2. Accountability & Ownership Clear ‚úì

- [ ] **Single owner identified for each workstream**
  - Major initiatives have clear owner
  - Owner is empowered to make decisions
  - Owner has resources they need
  - Owner is accountable for outcomes

- [ ] **Team structure designed for execution**
  - Organizational structure clear (who reports to whom)
  - Roles and responsibilities defined
  - Cross-functional dependencies identified
  - Decision-making authority established

- [ ] **Escalation and governance defined**
  - How often does leadership review progress?
  - What triggers escalation?
  - What are decision points?
  - How are conflicts resolved?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
ORGANIZATIONAL STRUCTURE:

Executive Sponsor: CEO
  ‚îú‚îÄ SMB Product Workstream Lead: VP Product (full authority over roadmap)
  ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ SMB Product Manager
  ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ 3 SMB Engineers
  ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ 1 Designer
  ‚îÇ
  ‚îî‚îÄ SMB GTM Workstream Lead: VP Sales (full authority over go-to-market)
      ‚îú‚îÄ SMB Sales Director
      ‚îú‚îÄ 3 SMB Account Executives
      ‚îî‚îÄ 1 SMB Marketing Lead

GOVERNANCE:
- Weekly steering committee (15 min): Exec sponsor + workstream leads
- Monthly board review (60 min): Full leadership team
- Quarterly gate reviews: Assess phase completion

ESCALATION:
- Routine decisions: Workstream lead authority
- >$100K spend: Exec sponsor approval
- Timeline delays >2 weeks: Escalate immediately
- Product/GTM conflicts: Exec sponsor decides
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Complete org chart
- ‚ùå Job descriptions for every role
- ‚ùå Hiring timeline
- ‚ùå Compensation/incentive design

---

### 3. Resource Requirements & Allocation ‚úì

- [ ] **Resource needs identified by phase**
  - People requirements (headcount, roles, timeline)
  - Budget requirements (capital, operating expenses)
  - Technology/infrastructure needs
  - Partner/vendor requirements

- [ ] **Resource constraints acknowledged**
  - Total available budget vs. needed budget
  - Total available people vs. needed people
  - Are we within constraints or do we need to negotiate?
  - Where are the tightest constraints?

- [ ] **Contingency and flexibility planned**
  - If resources are tighter than planned, what gets deprioritized?
  - If we have more resources than expected, what gets accelerated?
  - What's the minimum viable resource set?
  - What's the optimal resource set?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
RESOURCE REQUIREMENTS:

HEADCOUNT:
- Phase 1 (Months 0-6): 8 new hires (product/gtm core team)
- Phase 2 (Months 6-12): 5 additional (expand teams, customer success)
- Phase 3 (Months 12-24): 10+ (scale across all functions)
- Total Year 1: 13 new hires

BUDGET:
- Phase 1: $1.5M (hiring, tools, partnerships)
- Phase 2: $2M (product development, sales ramp)
- Phase 3: $3M (scale, marketing, customer success)
- Total Year 1: $6.5M

CONSTRAINTS:
- Available headcount budget: $10M across all initiatives (SMB is 13/50 total)
- ‚úì Headcount plan is feasible
- Available capital budget: $5M for investments
- ‚úó Budget shortfall: $1.5M in Year 1; need approval for incremental funding

CONTINGENCIES:
If budget cut 20% ($1.3M): Defer Phase 3 activities to Year 2
If we get 20% more budget: Accelerate to full team by Month 4
Minimum viable: 5 person team (product lead + 2 eng, sales lead + 1 ae)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Detailed budget line items
- ‚ùå Complete hiring plan
- ‚ùå Technology infrastructure specs
- ‚ùå Vendor contracts

---

### 4. Success Metrics & Tracking ‚úì

- [ ] **Success metrics defined for execution**
  - Business outcome metrics (revenue, profitability, retention)
  - Execution metrics (on-time delivery, quality, efficiency)
  - Leading indicators (pipeline, engagement, usage)
  - Frequency of tracking (daily, weekly, monthly)

- [ ] **Metrics connect to strategic objectives**
  - How do execution metrics serve strategic goal?
  - How will metrics inform course correction?
  - What's acceptable performance range?
  - What triggers intervention/escalation?

- [ ] **Targets are realistic and ambitious**
  - Targets are based on data and experience (not guesswork)
  - Targets are stretch (not easy to achieve)
  - Targets are achievable (not impossible)
  - Targets improve over time (Year 1 vs. Year 3)

**What This Looks Like:**
```
STRATEGIC OBJECTIVE: Build profitable SMB business to $15M ARR by Year 3

SUCCESS METRICS:

Product Development:
- MVP Launch: On time, quality <5 critical bugs at launch
- Feature Adoption: 60%+ users adopt simplified feature set within 3 months
- Customer Satisfaction: NPS >60 by end of Year 1

Sales & GTM:
- Sales Ramp: 3 AEs close $500K by Month 6, $300K/mo each by Month 12
- Partnership: 3-5 partners generating 20%+ of revenue by Year 2
- Customer Acquisition Cost: <12 month payback

Financial:
- Year 1 Revenue: $1M
- Year 2 Revenue: $8M
- Year 3 Revenue: $15M
- Gross Margin: >70% from day 1

Execution:
- Project Plans: On time delivery 80%+
- Quality: <3% customer escalations
- Team: Hiring on schedule; turnover <10%/year

TRACKING:
- Daily: Sales metrics (pipeline, activity)
- Weekly: Product metrics (development progress, customer feedback)
- Monthly: Financial review (revenue, expenses, cash)
- Quarterly: Strategic review (progress vs. plan, course correction)

INTERVENTION TRIGGERS:
- If revenue misses 20% vs. plan: Escalate to leadership; reassess GTM
- If customer churn >15%: Escalate to product; assess product-market fit
- If hiring delays >2 months: Escalate to CEO; identify barriers
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Detailed metric definitions
- ‚ùå Complete dashboard design
- ‚ùå All possible metrics (focus on key ones)
- ‚ùå Perfect forecasting

---

### 5. Innovation Integration ‚úì

- [ ] **Breakthrough opportunities integrated into plan**
  - Innovation ideas from INSIGHT/DECIDE surfaced
  - Which innovations are included in core plan?
  - Which innovations are in parallel/future tracks?
  - How are innovations resourced?

- [ ] **Innovation doesn't compromise core execution**
  - Core plan is solid (execution must happen)
  - Innovation adds to core (doesn't replace)
  - Innovation risks are mitigated
  - Resources for innovation are allocated separately

- [ ] **Pathways to breakthrough identified**
  - What does success look like for innovations?
  - How will we recognize if innovation is working?
  - What's the decision point to escalate or kill?
  - How do innovations feed into future phases?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
CORE PLAN: Build SMB product, establish GTM, reach $1M revenue Year 1

INNOVATION TRACKS:

Innovation 1: API-First Integration Marketplace
- Idea: Enable partners to build on our APIs; accelerate feature development
- How: Parallel track to core product; 2 engineers on marketplace
- When: Design Phase 1, build Phase 2, launch Phase 2 end
- Success: 5+ integration partners building by end of Year 1
- Decision Point: At Month 6, assess adoption and partner interest
- Future: If successful, expand to core business model by Year 2

Innovation 2: Usage-Based Pricing Pilot
- Idea: Align revenue with customer value created
- How: Parallel track; test with cohort of customers
- When: Design Phase 1, pilot Phase 2
- Success: Pilot cohort has higher NPS and retention
- Decision Point: At Month 9, assess pilot results
- Future: If successful, transition to usage-based for all SMB customers

RESOURCE ALLOCATION:
- Core Plan: 8 FTEs + $6.5M
- Innovation Tracks: 2 FTEs + $500K (separate, additive)
- Total: 10 FTEs + $7M

GOVERNANCE:
- Core plan: Monthly reviews, steering committee oversight
- Innovation: Quarterly reviews, separate approval for escalation
- If innovations threaten core plan: Pause innovation immediately
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Detailed innovation project plans
- ‚ùå Complete innovation business cases
- ‚ùå Guaranteed innovation success
- ‚ùå Entire innovation portfolio mapped

---

### 6. Risk Management & Contingencies ‚úì

- [ ] **Execution risks identified**
  - Resource risks (can we hire enough? retain people?)
  - Timeline risks (are estimates realistic?)
  - Market risks (will customers respond?)
  - Organizational risks (can we manage dual focus?)

- [ ] **Risk mitigation approaches defined**
  - For critical risks: What's our mitigation?
  - Is mitigation built into plan?
  - What's contingency if mitigation fails?
  - Who monitors this risk?

- [ ] **Contingency plans for critical scenarios**
  - If product development slips 3 months: What's plan B?
  - If SMB adoption slower than expected: How do we respond?
  - If competitor launches competitive offering: What's response?
  - What are go/no-go decision points?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
CRITICAL EXECUTION RISKS:

Risk 1: Can't hire/retain SMB team
- Probability: MEDIUM | Impact: HIGH (jeopardizes timeline)
- Mitigation: Hire early (month 1); offer competitive comp; clear vision
- Contingency: Outsource product to agency if hiring fails
- Go/No-Go: By Month 3, have SMB Product Lead; by Month 4, team core
- Monitor: Hiring pipeline monthly; retention metrics quarterly

Risk 2: Product development slips
- Probability: MEDIUM | Impact: MEDIUM (delays revenue, not fatal)
- Mitigation: Scope MVP ruthlessly; experienced team lead; frequent reviews
- Contingency: Extend Phase 1 by 3 months OR reduce feature scope
- Go/No-Go: By Month 6, must have MVP in customer testing
- Monitor: Development velocity weekly; customer feedback monthly

Risk 3: Sales adoption slower than expected
- Probability: HIGH | Impact: MEDIUM (revenue impact, fixable)
- Mitigation: Hire experienced SMB sales leader; clear incentives; early customer wins
- Contingency: Partner with integrators/resellers to fill gap
- Go/No-Go: By Month 6, AE must have first customer; by Month 12, $300K+ pipeline
- Monitor: Sales metrics weekly; pipeline health monthly

Risk 4: Dual focus distracts from enterprise
- Probability: MEDIUM | Impact: MEDIUM (enterprise churn risk)
- Mitigation: Separate teams; clear resource allocation; executive oversight
- Contingency: If enterprise loses customers, pause SMB scaling
- Go/No-Go: Monitor enterprise health monthly; threshold: >90% retention
- Monitor: Enterprise revenue/retention monthly; team satisfaction quarterly
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Complete risk register
- ‚ùå Detailed mitigation plans
- ‚ùå Comprehensive contingency plans
- ‚ùå Risk-free execution (some risk inevitable)

---

### 7. Stakeholder Alignment & Communication ‚úì

- [ ] **Key stakeholders aligned on plan**
  - Executive leadership understands plan
  - Board is informed and supportive (if relevant)
  - Sales/Product leadership understand their roles
  - Affected teams understand impact on them

- [ ] **Communication plan for organization**
  - How will plan be communicated to broader org?
  - What's the narrative (why this matters)?
  - Who delivers message (credible messenger)?
  - When and how frequently (ongoing)?

- [ ] **Stakeholder concerns surfaced and addressed**
  - What concerns did different groups raise?
  - How are we addressing legitimate concerns?
  - What trade-offs are we accepting?
  - How will we support affected teams?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
STAKEHOLDER ALIGNMENT:

CEO: Aligned on dual-segment strategy, understands 3-year plan, will sponsor
VP Product: Owns core product excellence, supports separate SMB team approach
VP Sales: Understands dual go-to-market, will support sales team independence
VP Finance: Approved $6.5M investment, understands ROI timeline
Board: Briefed on strategic rationale, supports 18-month test period

COMMUNICATION PLAN:

All-Hands (Week 1):
- Message: "Strategic opportunity in SMB market; we're building this systematically"
- Narrative: Enterprise success ‚Üí SMB opportunity ‚Üí how we'll serve both
- Messenger: CEO
- Format: Town hall presentation + Q&A

Sales Team (Week 1):
- Message: "New SMB offering coming; exciting growth opportunity"
- Narrative: Market opportunity, customer need, competitive threat
- Messenger: VP Sales + SMB Sales Lead
- Format: Team meeting + product roadmap sharing

Product Team (Week 1):
- Message: "New SMB team; here's how we'll maintain enterprise excellence"
- Narrative: Separate teams, clear ownership, no compromise on enterprise
- Messenger: VP Product + SMB Product Lead
- Format: Team meeting + organizational structure

CONCERN MITIGATION:

Sales Concern: "This will distract from enterprise"
‚Üí Response: Separate teams; enterprise team has dedicated resources; clear metrics to protect

Product Concern: "Can't do both well"
‚Üí Response: Product leads have autonomy; different technology stacks OK; clear handoff points

Finance Concern: "What if SMB doesn't work?"
‚Üí Response: Break-even in 18 months; no further investment if not hitting targets; contingency plan

ONGOING COMMUNICATION:
- Monthly: Leadership updates to all-hands
- Quarterly: Strategic review presentation to board
- Weekly: Core team standups
- Ad-hoc: Crisis communication if major issues
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Complete communications plan
- ‚ùå Every stakeholder handled
- ‚ùå Resolved all concerns
- ‚ùå Complete messaging library

---

### 8. Documentation & Handoff to Operations ‚úì

- [ ] **Comprehensive execution plan documented**
  - Phased plan with activities, owners, timelines
  - Critical path and dependencies clear
  - Resources and budget allocated
  - Risk mitigation and contingencies outlined

- [ ] **Success metrics dashboard prepared**
  - Key metrics defined and tracked
  - Targets established for each phase
  - Reporting cadence set
  - Dashboard or scorecard created

- [ ] **Organizational readiness package**
  - Team structure and roles
  - Decision-making authority
  - Escalation paths
  - Communication plan

- [ ] **Persona Handoff & Final Synthesis**
  - Complete strategic-to-execution journey captured
  - Decision rationale documented
  - Plan articulated clearly
  - Recommendations for ongoing refinement
  - Learning capture for future engagements

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Execution Plan:** 15-20 page detailed plan with phased activities, owners, timelines
- **Success Dashboard:** 1-page scorecard with key metrics, targets, tracking frequency
- **Org Structure Doc:** 2-3 page description of teams, roles, decision authority
- **Final Synthesis:** 5-page comprehensive document summarizing entire journey from problem to execution plan

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Beautifully formatted plans
- ‚ùå Complete project management tool setup
- ‚ùå Every detail specified
- ‚ùå Operational readiness (can begin with this foundation)

---

## Enhancing Criteria (Improving Quality)

These items strengthen the phase but aren't strictly blocking:

- [ ] **Quick wins identified**
  - What can we accomplish in 30/60/90 days?
  - What builds momentum and confidence?
  - What de-risks bigger initiatives?
  - What do we celebrate early?

- [ ] **Learning loops built in**
  - How will we capture lessons as we execute?
  - What will we test vs. implement at scale?
  - How do we stay adaptive to market feedback?
  - When do we pause and reassess?

- [ ] **Partner/vendor strategy outlined**
  - What partners do we need?
  - How will we engage them?
  - What are key partnerships for success?
  - What's partner timeline/process?

- [ ] **Change management approach sketched**
  - How will we help people adapt to changes?
  - What training/support will be needed?
  - How do we handle resistance?
  - What's the cultural shift required?

- [ ] **Financial model detailed**
  - Unit economics modeled
  - Path to profitability clear
  - Key financial assumptions identified
  - Sensitivity analysis on critical variables

---

## Quality Checks (Before Handoff)

Before confirming phase completion, ask yourself:

1. **Is this plan truly executable?**
   - Would a capable operations team understand what to do?
   - Are there any gaps or ambiguities?
   - Are resource needs realistic?
   - Is timeline achievable?

2. **Will we be able to track progress?**
   - Are success metrics clear?
   - Can we measure them?
   - Will we know if we're on track?
   - Will we catch problems early?

3. **Is the organization ready?**
   - Are teams aligned?
   - Do people understand their roles?
   - Will they have what they need?
   - Are risks and concerns addressed?

4. **Do we have a path forward if things go wrong?**
   - Are contingencies thoughtful?
   - Are decision points clear?
   - Will we know when to pivot?
   - Is there flexibility in the plan?

---

## Readiness Assessment

### ‚úÖ Ready to Execute When

All blocking criteria are met:
- Execution plan is detailed and sequenced
- Accountability and ownership are clear
- Resource requirements and allocation are defined
- Success metrics are realistic and tracked
- Innovation is integrated without compromising core plan
- Risks and contingencies are addressed
- Stakeholders are aligned
- Documentation and handoff to operations is complete

**The organization is ready to execute with confidence.**

---

### üîÑ Needs More Work When

One or more blocking criteria are unmet:

- **Plan too vague?**
  - ‚Üí Add more specificity to activities
  - ‚Üí Define clear success conditions
  - ‚Üí Establish ownership and timelines

- **Accountability unclear?**
  - ‚Üí Define single owner for each initiative
  - ‚Üí Clarify decision-making authority
  - ‚Üí Establish governance structure

- **Resources insufficient?**
  - ‚Üí Identify what would make resources adequate
  - ‚Üí Plan contingencies for resource constraints
  - ‚Üí Prioritize ruthlessly if needed

- **Success metrics weak?**
  - ‚Üí Define specific, measurable metrics
  - ‚Üí Connect metrics to strategic objectives
  - ‚Üí Establish realistic targets

- **Stakeholders not ready?**
  - ‚Üí Address concerns and objections
  - ‚Üí Build communication plan
  - ‚Üí Secure executive sponsorship

---

## What This Phase DOES Include

‚úÖ Detailed execution plan by phase
‚úÖ Activities, owners, timelines, success criteria
‚úÖ Clear accountability and org structure
‚úÖ Resource allocation and budget
‚úÖ Success metrics and tracking dashboard
‚úÖ Innovation integrated into plan
‚úÖ Risk mitigation and contingencies
‚úÖ Stakeholder alignment and communication plan
‚úÖ Complete documentation for operations team
‚úÖ Final synthesis of entire strategic journey

---

## What This Phase DOES NOT Include

‚ùå Detailed project schedules (Gantt charts)
‚ùå Individual job descriptions
‚ùå Complete organizational redesign
‚ùå Minute-by-minute operational details
‚ùå All future phases beyond Year 1
‚ùå Guaranteed execution success

---

## Common Blockers & How to Resolve

| Blocker | Signal | Resolution |
|---------|--------|-----------|
| **Plan too ambitious** | "We can't do all this" | Ruthlessly prioritize; defer non-critical items |
| **Resources too tight** | "We don't have enough people/budget" | Accept trade-offs; defer initiatives; seek approval |
| **Metrics too many** | "We're tracking 20 KPIs" | Focus on 5-7 key metrics; defer others |
| **Stakeholder misalignment** | "Sales doesn't support this" | Address concerns; clarify rationale; secure buy-in |
| **Innovation too vague** | "We can't measure innovation success" | Define specific metrics; test incrementally |
| **Risk overwhelming** | "What if this all fails?" | Accept some risk; focus mitigation on critical risks |
| **Timeline unrealistic** | "Six months? We can't..." | Extend timeline OR reduce scope ruthlessly |

---

## Post-Completion Actions

Once this checklist passes:

1. **Finalize Execution Plan Document**
   - All phases documented
   - Activities, owners, timelines clear
   - Critical path identified
   - Dependencies mapped

2. **Create Success Metrics Dashboard**
   - Key metrics identified
   - Targets set
   - Reporting cadence established
   - Dashboard template created

3. **Prepare Organizational Readiness Package**
   - Team structure documented
   - Roles and responsibilities
   - Decision-making authority
   - Governance structure

4. **Create Final Synthesis Document**
   - Entire strategic journey documented
   - Problem to execution connection clear
   - Key decisions and rationale
   - Recommendations for ongoing refinement

5. **Prepare Handoff Presentation**
   - Execution plan summarized
   - Key highlights and critical items
   - Roles and expectations
   - Next steps and first actions

6. **Hand Off to Operations Team**
   - Present execution plan to operational leadership
   - Confirm understanding and readiness
   - Establish operating rhythm/cadence
   - Begin execution

7. **Archive Complete Strategic Work**
   - All phases documented and saved
   - Decision journals captured
   - Key learnings noted
   - Foundation for future refinements

==================== START: analyse-phase-completion-checklist ====================
# ANALYSE Phase Completion Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that the ANALYSE phase (Strategic Analyst + Strategic Specialist) has completed all essential work before transitioning to the INSIGHT phase. This checklist ensures hypotheses have been systematically tested, data has been rigorously analyzed, and patterns have been identified that support strategic decision-making.

## What This Phase Accomplishes

The ANALYSE phase transforms hypotheses into evidence-based insights. The Analyst and Specialist together ensure:
- All key hypotheses are systematically tested
- Quantitative data supports findings
- Competitive landscape is understood
- Patterns and trends are identified
- Findings are documented with supporting evidence

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. Hypothesis Testing Completion ‚úì

- [ ] **All priority hypotheses have been tested**
  - High-impact hypotheses: all tested
  - Medium-impact hypotheses: all tested
  - Quick-win hypotheses: tested (or explicitly deferred with reason)
  - At least 80% of hypotheses from SPLIT phase tested

- [ ] **Testing evidence is documented**
  - For each hypothesis: data/evidence gathered
  - Testing methodology documented
  - Sample sizes adequate (or limitations noted)
  - Data sources credible and traceable

- [ ] **Hypotheses validated or refuted**
  - Each hypothesis has clear conclusion: supported, refuted, or inconclusive
  - Strength of evidence assessed (strong, moderate, weak)
  - Confidence level in conclusion noted
  - Boundary conditions identified (when hypothesis holds true)

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Hypothesis:** "SMB customers churn due to pricing"
  - **Testing:** Exit interviews (15 customers), pricing analysis (vs. 5 competitors), market research
  - **Evidence:** 12/15 exit interviews cited price; we're 20-30% higher than closest competitor; market research confirms price sensitivity in SMB
  - **Conclusion:** **STRONGLY SUPPORTED** - price is primary driver for SMB churn
  - **Boundary:** Applies to SMB segment <100 employees; enterprise less price sensitive

- **Hypothesis:** "Product mobile experience drives enterprise churn"
  - **Testing:** Feature gap analysis, NPS by device type, customer interviews
  - **Evidence:** Mobile is 15% of usage; desktop-only features not major complaint; NPS similar across device types
  - **Conclusion:** **REFUTED** - not a primary churn driver; secondary concern
  - **Alternative Found:** Enterprise customers want advanced integrations (API quality)

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Statistical significance testing
- ‚ùå Peer-reviewed academic rigor
- ‚ùå Testing of tangential hypotheses
- ‚ùå Proof beyond reasonable doubt (strong evidence is enough)

---

### 2. Quantitative Analysis ‚úì

- [ ] **Financial/business impact quantified**
  - Revenue impact of problem calculated (or estimated with confidence range)
  - Cost impact quantified where relevant
  - Customer impact measured (segment, volume, value)
  - Time-to-impact understood (when does this become critical?)

- [ ] **Market-level analysis completed**
  - Market size (TAM) estimated for relevant segments
  - Market growth rate identified
  - Market trends documented
  - Competitive market dynamics understood

- [ ] **Performance baselines established**
  - Current state metrics captured
  - Industry/competitor benchmarks found
  - Performance gaps quantified
  - Historical trends analyzed (if available)

- [ ] **Financial models created (if applicable)**
  - Cost/benefit models for problem understanding
  - Sensitivity analysis on key variables
  - Scenarios modeled (best/worst/likely case)
  - Assumptions documented and validated

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Financial Impact:** We're losing $5M ARR to churn; competitor pricing costs us 12-15% of SMB revenue; market is growing at 25% annually but we're growing at 8%
- **Market Analysis:** $2B addressable SMB market; 5 major competitors; market consolidating around feature-rich solutions
- **Performance Gap:** We're priced 25% above market average; NPS 15 points below competitors; customer retention is 85% vs. 95% industry average
- **Models:** NPV of $50M opportunity if we reduce churn by 5%; breakeven in 18 months on pricing change

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect data
- ‚ùå Multiple years of trend data
- ‚ùå Complex financial modeling
- ‚ùå Competitive intelligence on every competitor

---

### 3. Competitive Analysis ‚úì

- [ ] **Competitive landscape mapped**
  - Direct competitors identified (3-5 main ones)
  - Indirect competitors/substitutes identified
  - Competitive positioning compared (features, pricing, positioning)
  - Competitive advantages and disadvantages assessed

- [ ] **Competitive differentiation understood**
  - Where we're stronger than competitors
  - Where competitors are stronger
  - Defensibility of advantages assessed
  - Gaps in market (unmet needs) identified

- [ ] **Competitive threats and opportunities identified**
  - New competitive threats emerging (or not)
  - Competitive vulnerabilities to exploit
  - Possible competitive responses to our actions
  - Strategic positioning implications

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Competitive Landscape:** 4 main competitors; Company X is market leader (40% share); we're #3 (15% share)
- **Feature Comparison:**
  - Us vs. Competitor X: They have mobile app (we don't); we have better integrations; they're faster to deploy
  - Pricing: We're 25% higher; they have aggressive SMB pricing
- **Differentiation:** Our strength is enterprise features; weakness is SMB pricing; opportunity is integration ecosystem
- **Threat:** Company X launching SMB pricing tier; Opportunity: their complexity alienates SMB segment

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Every competitor analyzed in detail
- ‚ùå Sales intelligence on competitive pricing
- ‚ùå Predictive competitive strategy
- ‚ùå Patent analysis or technology depth

---

### 4. Pattern Recognition & Insights ‚úì

- [ ] **Data patterns identified**
  - Trends found in customer behavior data
  - Correlations identified (and causation assessed)
  - Anomalies or outliers explained
  - Patterns by segment, geography, time period, etc.

- [ ] **Root causes confirmed or revised**
  - SPLIT phase hypotheses validated against data
  - Root causes now grounded in evidence
  - Previously hidden drivers discovered
  - Root cause ranking by impact established

- [ ] **Key insights documented**
  - Major findings clearly stated
  - Supporting evidence provided
  - Implications for strategy captured
  - Questions answered from SPLIT phase

- [ ] **Systemic understanding developed**
  - How different factors interact understood
  - Feedback loops identified
  - Leverage points identified (where to apply pressure for change)
  - Ripple effects of different causes understood

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Patterns:** SMB customers churn after 18 months when they outgrow basic features; Enterprise customers more stable (3+ year retention)
- **Root Causes (Refined):**
  - Primary: Pricing misalignment for SMB segment (60% of churn)
  - Secondary: Feature gaps for growing SMB (30% of churn)
  - Tertiary: Competitive displacement (10% of churn)
- **Insight:** We're winning the customer acquisition battle but losing mid-market customers to scale-up competitor offering; we need pricing flexibility strategy
- **Leverage Point:** If we create SMB-specific pricing tier, we could retain 60% of churning customers; incremental revenue $3M+

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfectly explained variance
- ‚ùå Complete causal proof
- ‚ùå Statistical models
- ‚ùå Predictive analytics

---

### 5. Data Quality & Rigor ‚úì

- [ ] **Data sources credible and documented**
  - Sources identified for all major findings
  - Data quality assessed (clean, representative, timely)
  - Data limitations acknowledged
  - Proxy data or estimation noted where actual data unavailable

- [ ] **Analytical methodology transparent**
  - How data was analyzed explained
  - Tools/methods used documented
  - Analysis choices justified
  - Validation of findings (did we check our work?)

- [ ] **Assumptions explicit**
  - All major assumptions documented
  - Why assumptions were made (data gap, industry standard, expert judgment)
  - Risk if assumptions wrong assessed
  - Sensitivity to assumptions tested (where critical)

- [ ] **Confidence levels communicated**
  - Which findings are high-confidence (strong evidence)
  - Which are moderate-confidence (reasonable evidence, some gaps)
  - Which are exploratory/indicative (emerging pattern)
  - Caveats and limitations clearly stated

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Data Sources:** Customer churn data (CRM, validated against accounting); exit interviews (15 customers, purposive sample); competitive pricing (public websites, customer reports); market research (3rd-party report, 2 years old)
- **Methodology:** Churn analysis (SQL queries, triangulated across 3 sources); exit interviews (open-ended, coded for themes); competitive analysis (feature matrix, pricing sheets); market research (secondary)
- **Assumptions:** Exit interviews represent larger population (acknowledged bias toward more engaged customers); pricing data reflects public pricing only (actual deals likely different)
- **Confidence Levels:**
  - HIGH: SMB churn rates by cohort (internal data, clean)
  - MODERATE: Price sensitivity (exit interviews, market data, but small sample)
  - EXPLORATORY: Enterprise feature needs (few interviews, anecdotal evidence)

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Primary research on all hypotheses
- ‚ùå Peer review of analysis
- ‚ùå Academic-level rigor
- ‚ùå Perfect data or methodology

---

### 6. Analysis Coherence & Completeness ‚úì

- [ ] **All problem components addressed**
  - Each branch of problem tree analyzed
  - All questions from SPLIT phase answered (or explicitly noted as unanswered)
  - No major analytical gaps
  - Cross-component analysis done (how components interact)

- [ ] **Analysis answers strategic questions**
  - Root cause analysis addresses "why" questions
  - Market analysis answers "how big/important" questions
  - Competitive analysis answers "relative position" questions
  - Together, analysis informs strategic choices

- [ ] **Findings are actionable**
  - Analysis results lead to clear implications
  - Not just data for data's sake
  - Connects back to original problem and success criteria
  - Informs next phase (INSIGHT) thinking

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Original Problem:** Why are we losing customers?
- **Analysis Addresses:**
  - Root causes (pricing, features, competition)
  - Market dynamics (growing segment churning; stable segment loyal)
  - Competitive positioning (we're premium player losing to value players)
  - Financial impact (quantified revenue at risk)
- **Actionable Result:** Clear understanding of churn drivers; implication is need to segment strategy (premium for enterprise, value for SMB)

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Analysis of every possible angle
- ‚ùå Answers to questions outside original scope
- ‚ùå Recommendations or solutions
- ‚ùå Complete clarity on all factors

---

### 7. Documentation & Handoff ‚úì

- [ ] **Analysis summary document created**
  - Executive summary of key findings
  - Findings by problem component
  - Evidence for major conclusions
  - Confidence levels stated
  - Caveats and limitations noted

- [ ] **Supporting analysis documents prepared**
  - Detailed findings by analysis area (competitive, financial, etc.)
  - Data sources and methodology documented
  - Visualizations (charts, matrices) created where helpful
  - Raw data referenced or archived

- [ ] **Persona Handoff document created**
  - Key findings highlighted
  - Hypotheses status summarized
  - Root causes confirmed/refined
  - Implications for next phase (INSIGHT)
  - Unanswered questions noted
  - Additional analysis if conducted noted

- [ ] **All work organized and accessible**
  - Analysis organized by finding area
  - Data sources documented
  - Methodology explained
  - Metadata captured (when conducted, by whom, confidence levels)

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Analysis Summary:** 5-7 page document with findings, evidence, confidence levels, caveats
- **Supporting Documents:** Competitive analysis matrix; financial impact models; churn analysis by cohort; customer interview themes
- **Handoff Document:** 2-3 page summary of key findings, root causes, what it means, what Communicator should focus on
- **Archives:** Raw data, analysis notebooks/spreadsheets, interview transcripts, source documents

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Publication-ready presentations
- ‚ùå Every analysis variable documented
- ‚ùå Perfectly organized knowledge base
- ‚ùå Polished deliverables (good enough for internal use)

---

## Enhancing Criteria (Improving Quality)

These items strengthen the phase but aren't strictly blocking:

- [ ] **Customer segment analysis completed**
  - Churn rates analyzed by segment (company size, industry, geography, tenure)
  - Different root causes by segment identified
  - Segment-specific recommendations emerging
  - High-priority segments identified

- [ ] **Trend analysis conducted**
  - Is churn increasing, decreasing, stable?
  - Are competitive threats accelerating?
  - Are market dynamics shifting?
  - Leading indicators of future churn identified

- [ ] **Scenario planning initiated**
  - Best case scenario articulated (what if we fix all root causes?)
  - Worst case scenario articulated (what if trends accelerate?)
  - Most likely scenario described
  - Financial impact of each scenario modeled

- [ ] **Cross-functional validation completed**
  - Key findings reviewed with relevant business leaders
  - Disagreements surfaced and explored
  - Different perspectives integrated
  - Organizational buy-in beginning to form

- [ ] **Emerging opportunities identified**
  - Beyond just fixing problems, growth opportunities spotted
  - Competitive positioning improvements possible
  - Customer value creation possibilities seen
  - Innovation ideas emerging from data

---

## Quality Checks (Before Handoff)

Before confirming phase completion, ask yourself:

1. **Have we thoroughly tested the hypotheses?**
   - Did we find evidence for each major hypothesis?
   - Did we consider alternative explanations?
   - Would the findings hold up to scrutiny?

2. **Does the analysis answer the original questions?**
   - Can we explain why the problem exists?
   - Do we understand the business impact?
   - Can we identify root causes vs. symptoms?

3. **Is the analysis actionable?**
   - Do findings point toward possible solutions?
   - Can we understand what to fix?
   - Are priorities clear?

4. **Do the Analyst and Specialist both feel the analysis is complete?**
   - Do they have confidence in findings?
   - Are there nagging doubts or gaps?
   - Are they ready to hand off?

---

## Readiness Assessment

### ‚úÖ Ready to Proceed to INSIGHT When

All blocking criteria are met:
- All priority hypotheses are systematically tested
- Quantitative analysis is completed and documented
- Competitive landscape is understood
- Root causes are confirmed through evidence
- Data quality and limitations are transparent
- Findings are complete and actionable
- Documentation is ready for handoff

**The Communicator will have solid evidence-based findings to synthesize into insights.**

---

### üîÑ Needs More Work When

One or more blocking criteria are unmet:

- **Hypotheses not fully tested?**
  - ‚Üí Identify which hypotheses remain untested
  - ‚Üí Assess if testing is feasible and critical
  - ‚Üí Plan additional testing or defer with clear rationale

- **Data gaps too large?**
  - ‚Üí Identify what data is missing and why
  - ‚Üí Assess feasibility of gathering
  - ‚Üí Document assumptions filling gaps
  - ‚Üí Note as limitation in confidence level

- **Analysis lacks rigor?**
  - ‚Üí Review methodology with Specialist
  - ‚Üí Strengthen validation of findings
  - ‚Üí Document limitations more clearly
  - ‚Üí Reassess confidence levels

- **Findings don't connect to problem?**
  - ‚Üí Return to original problem statement
  - ‚Üí Check that all components addressed
  - ‚Üí Identify analysis gaps
  - ‚Üí Ensure findings directly inform understanding

---

## What This Phase DOES Include

‚úÖ Hypothesis testing and validation
‚úÖ Quantitative analysis and financial modeling
‚úÖ Competitive landscape mapping
‚úÖ Root cause confirmation (evidence-based)
‚úÖ Pattern recognition and trend analysis
‚úÖ Data quality assessment and documentation
‚úÖ Confidence levels and caveats
‚úÖ Supporting evidence and methodology
‚úÖ Actionable findings ready for synthesis

---

## What This Phase DOES NOT Include

‚ùå Insights or synthesis (that's INSIGHT)
‚ùå Narratives or stories (that's STORY)
‚ùå Recommendations or solutions (that's DECIDE)
‚ùå Implementation planning (that's ACT)
‚ùå Innovation or breakthrough thinking (primary focus of later phases)

---

## Common Blockers & How to Resolve

| Blocker | Signal | Resolution |
|---------|--------|-----------|
| **Hypotheses incomplete** | Some untested | Prioritize critical ones; defer exploratory; document why |
| **Data unavailable** | "We don't have that" | Use proxies, conduct interviews, make assumptions explicit |
| **Analysis scattered** | No coherent narrative | Create summary document pulling findings together |
| **Findings unclear** | "Multiple possible interpretations" | Narrow down through additional analysis or expert judgment |
| **Confidence too low** | "We're not sure about this" | Accept lower confidence if data not available; note as limitation |
| **Over-analysis** | "We could keep analyzing forever" | Define minimal evidence needed; establish stop-point; move forward |

---

## Post-Completion Actions

Once this checklist passes:

1. **Create Analysis Summary Document**
   - Executive summary of findings
   - Key hypotheses and status
   - Root causes with supporting evidence
   - Competitive positioning
   - Financial impact

2. **Prepare Supporting Materials**
   - Detailed analysis by area
   - Methodology and data sources
   - Visualizations and charts
   - Raw data/transcripts archived

3. **Create Persona Handoff**
   - Use `persona-handoff-template.md`
   - Summarize key findings
   - Note root causes (confirmed)
   - Highlight what's clear vs. uncertain
   - Identify implications for next phase

4. **Coordinate with Communicator**
   - Share analysis summary
   - Prepare for synthesis phase
   - Identify key insights to emphasize
   - Note findings that need careful messaging

5. **Hand off to Strategic Communicator**
   - Share all analysis documents
   - Confirm Communicator ready to synthesize
   - Load INSIGHT phase files

6. **Archive ANALYSE Materials**
   - Save all analysis and data
   - Document methodologies
   - Reference for future phases

---

## Notes & Observations

Use this space to capture phase-specific insights:

- **What surprised us about the data?**

- **What was challenging to analyze?**

- **Customer insights not captured in findings?**

- **For future engagements:**

---

==================== START: business-model-canvas-validation-checklist ====================
# Business Model Canvas Validation Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that a completed Business Model Canvas documents all nine essential elements of a business model with clear logic, coherent relationships, and actionable insights.

## What Gets Validated

**Template Reference:** `templates/business-model-canvas-strategic.md`

**Used In:** INSIGHT and ACT phases for business model design and innovation

**Audience:** Strategic team, product leadership, operations

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. All Nine Elements Are Addressed ‚úì

- [ ] **Value Proposition: Clear and compelling**
  - What value does solution provide?
  - Why is it better than alternatives?
  - What problems does it solve?
  - What jobs does it do for customer?

- [ ] **Customer Segments: Specific and prioritized**
  - Who are primary customer segments?
  - What's different about each segment?
  - Which segments are priorities?
  - What segment dynamics matter?

- [ ] **Revenue Streams: Clear and credible**
  - How do we make money?
  - What's pricing model?
  - What's revenue per customer type?
  - How do customers pay?

- [ ] **Cost Structure: Complete and realistic**
  - What are major cost categories?
  - What drives costs?
  - What's cost per customer?
  - How do costs scale?

- [ ] **Key Resources: Essential assets identified**
  - What physical, intellectual, human resources needed?
  - What partnerships are essential?
  - What technology is critical?
  - What talent is required?

- [ ] **Key Activities: Critical operations defined**
  - What must we do to deliver value?
  - What are core activities?
  - What activities create competitive advantage?
  - What's the critical path?

- [ ] **Key Partnerships: Strategic relationships documented**
  - Who do we need to partner with?
  - Why are partnerships important?
  - What dependencies exist?
  - How do partnerships create value?

- [ ] **Customer Relationships: How we engage**
  - How do we acquire customers?
  - How do we retain customers?
  - What's customer lifecycle?
  - How do we create loyalty?

- [ ] **Channels: How we reach and serve customers**
  - How do customers discover us?
  - How do customers buy?
  - How do we deliver value?
  - How do we support customers?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
VALUE PROPOSITION: "Enterprise-grade integration platform that's
easy to use and fast to deploy. Helps companies sync data across
their technology ecosystem without building custom integrations."

CUSTOMER SEGMENTS:
- Enterprise (Fortune 500, $50K+ contracts, 5-year relationships)
- Mid-market (1000-10K employees, $10-50K contracts, 2-3 year relationships)
- SMB (100-1000 employees, $1-5K contracts, 1-2 year relationships)

REVENUE STREAMS:
- Subscription (primary): $1K-50K annually per customer
- Professional services: Integration/implementation
- Support/SLA: Premium support tier

COST STRUCTURE:
- Cloud infrastructure: 15% of revenue
- Customer support: 20% of revenue
- Product development: 30% of revenue
- Sales/marketing: 25% of revenue
- G&A/overhead: 10% of revenue

KEY RESOURCES:
- Engineering team (platform expertise)
- Pre-built integration library (90+ integrations)
- Cloud infrastructure (scalable, reliable)
- Sales team (enterprise sales expertise)
- Customer success team

KEY ACTIVITIES:
- Product development (maintain and improve platform)
- Integration development (build new integrations)
- Sales (enterprise sales motion)
- Customer success (ensure customer value realization)
- Support (technical support, troubleshooting)

KEY PARTNERSHIPS:
- Cloud providers (AWS, Azure)
- Integration partners (companies we integrate with)
- Channel partners (resellers, consultants)
- Technology partners (APIs, data sources)

CUSTOMER RELATIONSHIPS:
- Sales: Account executive-led for enterprise
- Implementation: Dedicated implementation team
- Ongoing support: Technical support; customer success check-ins
- Community: User conference, online community

CHANNELS:
- Direct sales (for enterprise)
- Website and self-serve (for SMB)
- Partnerships and resellers (for certain segments)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect completeness
- ‚ùå Detailed specifications
- ‚ùå All edge cases covered
- ‚ùå Complete financial modeling

---

### 2. Elements Are Internally Coherent ‚úì

- [ ] **Value proposition aligns with customer segments**
  - Does VP matter to customer segment?
  - Would segment willingly pay?
  - Does VP address customer needs?
  - Is it credible to customer?

- [ ] **Revenue model supports value proposition**
  - Do customers see value worth price?
  - Is pricing aligned with value?
  - Can customer afford it?
  - Does revenue model work financially?

- [ ] **Cost structure supports delivery**
  - Can we deliver value at this cost?
  - Do costs align with activities required?
  - Is profit margin achievable?
  - Are costs sustainable at scale?

- [ ] **Resources and activities support execution**
  - Do we have resources needed?
  - Can resources execute activities?
  - Are partnerships realistic?
  - Can we attract/retain talent?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
COHERENCE CHECK:

VALUE PROPOSITION: Easy-to-use integration platform
CUSTOMER SEGMENT: Enterprise companies
Question: Do enterprise customers value "easy to use"?
Answer: Yes, but only if feature-rich. Easy-to-use AND powerful
required for enterprise. Does our positioning deliver both?
Assessment: YES - we're "easy compared to custom" but also feature-rich

REVENUE MODEL: $50K annual subscription for enterprise
Question: Is this price aligned with value?
Analysis: Customer ROI = save $200K+ annually on developer time
Value = 4-10x cost. Price is aligned with value.
Assessment: YES - pricing is defensible

COST STRUCTURE: 20% on customer support for enterprise
Question: Can we support enterprise customers profitably?
Analysis: Enterprise customers need high-touch support.
Support cost may need to be 20-25% for enterprise.
At $50K revenue, that's $10K support cost = acceptable.
Assessment: YES - margins still healthy even with high support cost

RESOURCES/ACTIVITIES: 90+ pre-built integrations
Question: Do we have resources to maintain this?
Analysis: 10-person engineering team.
Maintaining 90 integrations = significant ongoing work.
Is this sustainable? Only if integrations are high-demand
and customer success shows value (justifying investment).
Assessment: OKAY - but need to monitor resource drain

OVERALL ASSESSMENT: Model is internally coherent.
All pieces support each other. No major contradictions.
Model is viable if execution meets plan.
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect alignment across all elements
- ‚ùå Detailed financial validation
- ‚ùå Complete capability assessment
- ‚ùå Perfect logic (some tension OK if understood)

---

### 3. Business Model Logic Is Explicit ‚úì

- [ ] **How do elements interact explained**
  - How does each element support others?
  - Where are dependencies?
  - What's the cause-and-effect?
  - Is logic clear?

- [ ] **Customer value creation is visible**
  - How do customers benefit?
  - How does each element contribute?
  - What's the path from activities to customer value?
  - Would customer understand logic?

- [ ] **Competitive positioning is clear**
  - How is our model different?
  - What's hard to copy?
  - What's our defensible advantage?
  - How do we stay ahead?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
BUSINESS MODEL LOGIC:

CUSTOMER VALUE CREATION:
1. We identify what integrations customer needs (customer research)
2. We pre-build those integrations (key activity)
3. We provide simple UI to configure them (key activity)
4. Customer can sync data in hours, not months (value delivered)
5. Customer saves $200K+ on developer time (value monetized)
6. Customer pays $30K for solution (our revenue)

ELEMENT INTERACTIONS:
Customer Segments ‚Üí Value Prop ‚Üí Revenue Model
Enterprise needs powerful + easy = $50K price
SMB needs simple + affordable = $1K price
(Same product, different positioning, different pricing)

Resources ‚Üí Activities ‚Üí Value Prop
90+ integrations (resource) + easy UI (activity) = less developer work
Engineering team (resource) + continuous improvement (activity) = platform reliability
Sales team (resource) + enterprise motion (activity) = customer acquisition

Partnerships ‚Üí Customer Relationships
Cloud partners (partnerships) enable reliability (customer relationship)
Integration partners (partnerships) enable ecosystem (customer value)
Reseller partners (partnerships) reach new segments (channels)

COMPETITIVE POSITIONING:
Hard to copy: 90+ pre-built integrations (took years to build)
Our advantage: Network effect (more integrations = more valuable)
Market position: "Most integrations" = competitive moat
Long-term: As we add integrations, we become harder to beat

COST STRUCTURE enables business model:
To maintain 90 integrations and support enterprise
We need 30% of revenue in product/engineering
That leaves 40% gross margin for other costs
At scale, model is profitable (gross margin > operating costs)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect cause-and-effect
- ‚ùå Detailed interdependency maps
- ‚ùå Mathematical modeling
- ‚ùå Complete competitive analysis

---

### 4. Model Is Realistic and Achievable ‚úì

- [ ] **Elements are realistic**
  - Can we actually build this?
  - Do partnerships exist/are feasible?
  - Can we acquire/retain talent?
  - Is market response likely?

- [ ] **Unit economics work**
  - Gross margin is healthy?
  - CAC payback is reasonable?
  - LTV is attractive?
  - Model scales profitably?

- [ ] **Key assumptions identified**
  - What must be true for model to work?
  - What are risky assumptions?
  - What would break the model?
  - How would we validate?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
REALISM CHECK:

Can we build 90 integrations?
Assessment: Yes, and we have. This is proven.

Can we maintain them as platforms change?
Assessment: Yes, with dedicated team. This is built into cost model.

Will customers pay $30K for SMB offering?
Assessment: Moderate confidence. SMB is price sensitive.
We'd need to prove value = 10x cost. Possible but not certain.

Will enterprise partnerships work?
Assessment: Yes. We have some partners already.
Path is clear.

UNIT ECONOMICS:

Customer: Enterprise
Revenue: $30K annual
Gross margin: 70% ($21K)
CAC: $5K (assume 3-6 month payback; healthy for enterprise SaaS)
LTV: $100K+ (3+ year relationship; high margin = strong value)
LTV:CAC: 20:1 (excellent)

Assessment: Unit economics are strong for enterprise

Customer: SMB
Revenue: $2K annual
Gross margin: 60% ($1.2K) - lower because less economies of scale
CAC: $500 (need to be efficient; possibly channel-based)
LTV: $8K (4 year relationship; best case)
LTV:CAC: 16:1 (good, but tighter than enterprise)

Assessment: Unit economics are acceptable for SMB if CAC can be controlled

KEY ASSUMPTIONS:

Assumption 1: Enterprise willing to pay $30K for pre-built integrations
Why: Saves developer time ($200K+ annual value)
Risk: If value not realized, price pressure
Mitigation: Customer success ensures value realization

Assumption 2: SMB willing to pay $2K for simplified solution
Why: Easy to use + key integrations = value
Risk: If SMB market is too price-sensitive, won't work
Mitigation: Validate willingness to pay before heavy investment

Assumption 3: We can maintain 90 integrations efficiently
Why: Built cost into model (20% of revenue)
Risk: If maintenance costs higher, margins compress
Mitigation: Monitor actual vs. planned; reduce integrations if needed

Assumption 4: Customers stick around (low churn)
Why: Switching costs and value stickiness
Risk: If churn higher than modeled, LTV drops
Mitigation: Monitor churn; improve customer success if needed
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect achievability assessment
- ‚ùå Complete market validation
- ‚ùå Detailed financial models
- ‚ùå Risk-free assumptions

---

### 5. Model Evolves Based on Market Learning ‚úì

- [ ] **Adaptation strategy is clear**
  - How will we know if model working?
  - When would we pivot?
  - What's the learning approach?
  - How do we stay flexible?

- [ ] **Contingencies identified**
  - If assumption 1 breaks, what do we do?
  - If assumption 2 breaks, what do we do?
  - Are there fallback positions?
  - Can we adjust model mid-course?

- [ ] **Scalability path is visible**
  - How does model scale with revenue?
  - Do unit economics improve at scale?
  - Are there scalability challenges?
  - How do we plan for scaling?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
EVOLUTION & LEARNING:

Measurement Approach:
Monthly: Track unit economics by customer segment
- CAC actual vs. plan
- LTV actual vs. plan
- Churn rate (overall and by segment)
- Customer satisfaction

Quarterly: Assess model assumptions
- Are customer segments behaving as expected?
- Is pricing right?
- Are partnerships working?
- Are activities supporting value prop?

Pivot Triggers:
IF SMB adoption is 50%+ slower than plan
AND financial projections miss by 25%+
THEN reassess SMB strategy (continue, pivot, or stop)

IF Enterprise churn rises above 10% (vs. 5% planned)
THEN investigate (product? support? competition?)
and adjust business model if needed

ADAPTATION OPTIONS:

If SMB market is less receptive than expected:
- Adjust pricing (lower to increase adoption)
- Simplify feature set further (reduce cost)
- Refocus on enterprise (proven segment)
- Pivot to adjacent segment (mid-market)

If integration maintenance is more expensive:
- Build API platform (let partners build integrations)
- Reduce number of integrations (focus on key ones)
- Adopt third-party integration marketplace
- Increase customer success cost and prices

SCALABILITY:

Current model (100 customers, $2M revenue):
- 30 engineers for product/integrations
- 10 customer success team
- 15 sales/marketing
- Gross margin: 65-70%
- Operating margin: Break-even to slight positive

Scaled model (1000 customers, $30M revenue):
- 50 engineers (not 300) due to automation/leverage
- 50 customer success (not 100) due to self-serve
- 50 sales/marketing (not 150) due to efficiency
- Gross margin: 70-75% (improve through scale)
- Operating margin: 30%+ (profitable at scale)

Assessment: Model scales well. Margins improve.
Not capital-intensive. Good unit economics at scale.
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect contingency plans
- ‚ùå Detailed learning metrics
- ‚ùå Complete scalability modeling
- ‚ùå Predictive accuracy

---

### 6. Documentation Quality ‚úì

- [ ] **Canvas is visually clear**
  - Nine elements clearly labeled
  - Relationships visible
  - Easy to understand at a glance
  - Professional appearance

- [ ] **Supporting narrative is complete**
  - Each element explained
  - Coherence articulated
  - Key logic explained
  - Assumptions documented

- [ ] **Appropriate level of detail**
  - Sufficient to understand model
  - Not so detailed it's overwhelming
  - Supports decision-making
  - Can be shared with stakeholders

**What This Looks Like:**
```
STRUCTURE:

Visual Canvas (1 page):
- Nine boxes/sections clearly labeled
- Key points in each box
- Visual flow showing relationships
- Professional formatting

Supporting Narrative (3-5 pages):
1. Business Model Overview
2. Element Explanations (1-2 sentences each)
3. Coherence Assessment (how elements work together)
4. Unit Economics Summary
5. Key Assumptions
6. Adaptation Strategy

Total: 1 page visual + 4 pages narrative = 5 pages
Scannable and useful for decision-making
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Beautiful graphic design
- ‚ùå Colorful visualizations
- ‚ùå Detailed financial models
- ‚ùå Complete appendices

---

## Enhancing Criteria (Improving Quality)

These items strengthen the canvas but aren't strictly blocking:

- [ ] **Competitive comparison**
  - How our model compares to competitors
  - What's different about our approach
  - What's hard for competitors to copy
  - Long-term defensibility clear

- [ ] **Financial model detail**
  - 3-year unit economics modeled
  - Sensitivity to key variables
  - Scaling economics clear
  - Profitability path visible

- [ ] **Customer validation**
  - Model grounded in customer research
  - Customer perspective captured
  - Willingness to pay validated
  - Value proposition confirmed

- [ ] **Scenario planning**
  - What if market grows 2x faster?
  - What if adoption is 50% slower?
  - What if competitor enters?
  - How resilient is model?

---

## Quality Checks

Before confirming canvas is complete, ask yourself:

1. **Does this capture the complete business model?**
   - All nine elements addressed?
   - Model makes sense holistically?
   - Are relationships clear?
   - Could someone understand without explanation?

2. **Is the model coherent?**
   - Do elements support each other?
   - Are there contradictions?
   - Would this work in practice?
   - Are there obvious flaws?

3. **Is the model realistic?**
   - Can we actually execute this?
   - Are unit economics viable?
   - Are assumptions credible?
   - Would investors fund this?

4. **Would this guide decisions?**
   - Does it clarify choices?
   - Does it highlight risks?
   - Does it show scalability?
   - Is it actionable?

---

## Readiness Assessment

### ‚úÖ Canvas is Ready When

All blocking criteria are met:
- All nine elements are addressed
- Elements are internally coherent
- Business model logic is explicit
- Model is realistic and achievable
- Model evolves based on learning
- Documentation quality is good

**Canvas can guide business model decisions.**

---

## Common Issues & Resolution

| Issue | Signal | Resolution |
|-------|--------|-----------|
| **Elements incomplete** | "Some boxes are empty" | Complete all nine elements |
| **Incoherent logic** | "These don't fit together" | Clarify how elements support each other |
| **Unrealistic** | "This won't work" | Validate assumptions; adjust model |
| **Too complex** | "Can't understand it" | Simplify; focus on key elements |
| **No numbers** | "How much does this cost?" | Add unit economics; quantify |
| **Too abstract** | "What does this actually mean?" | Provide concrete examples |

---

## Post-Validation Actions

Once this checklist passes:

1. **Validate with Key Stakeholders**
   - Share canvas with leadership
   - Get feedback on realism
   - Address concerns/questions
   - Refine based on input

2. **Test Key Assumptions**
   - Customer willingness to pay
   - Feasibility of partnerships
   - Resource requirements
   - Market responsiveness

3. **Use for Strategy & Planning**
   - Reference for decisions
   - Use for contingency planning
   - Track actual vs. model
   - Adapt as learning occurs

4. **Archive & Evolve**
   - Save original canvas
   - Version as changes occur
   - Document pivots/evolution
   - Use for learning

---
