==================== START: define-phase-completion-checklist ====================
# DEFINE Phase Completion Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that the DEFINE phase (Strategic Analyst) has completed all essential work before transitioning to the SPLIT phase. This checklist ensures the problem or opportunity is sufficiently clarified, quantified, and documented for productive strategic decomposition.

## What This Phase Accomplishes

The DEFINE phase transforms vague business challenges into clearly articulated, measurable problems ready for systematic analysis. The Strategic Analyst ensures we understand:
- What the problem/opportunity actually is
- Why it matters (business impact)
- Who is affected
- How we'll measure success

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. Problem/Opportunity Clarity ‚úì

- [ ] **Problem/opportunity is clearly articulated**
  - User can describe it in 1-2 sentences without ambiguity
  - Core issue is distinct from symptoms
  - Scope boundaries are defined (what's in/out of scope)

- [ ] **Business context is documented**
  - Current market/competitive landscape captured
  - Organizational context understood (size, structure, capabilities)
  - Strategic priorities that this addresses identified
  - Relevant stakeholder landscape outlined

- [ ] **Problem has quantifiable impact**
  - Financial impact estimated (revenue at risk, cost, margin impact)
  - Scope measured in business terms (market size, customer count, process volume)
  - Time sensitivity established (when does this need to be addressed?)
  - Baseline metrics captured (current state measurement)

**What This Looks Like:**
- "We're losing 15% of customers annually to competitor X, costing us $5M in ARR. We need to understand why and develop competitive response strategy."
- NOT: "We have competitive challenges"

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Root cause analysis
- ‚ùå Detailed competitive intelligence
- ‚ùå Complete market data
- ‚ùå Precise impact calculation

---

### 2. Success Criteria & Target State ‚úì

- [ ] **Success criteria are explicitly defined**
  - At least 3 measurable success metrics identified
  - Each metric has a target (not just direction)
  - Metrics are outcome-focused, not activity-focused
  - Success is testable and observable

- [ ] **Target state is articulated**
  - Desired future state described
  - What "solved" looks like for stakeholders
  - Constraints and realities acknowledged
  - Difference between current and target is clear

**What This Looks Like:**
- Success Metric 1: "Reduce customer churn from 15% to 5% annually"
- Success Metric 2: "Achieve 80% Net Promoter Score (vs. 62% current)"
- Success Metric 3: "Develop defensible competitive differentiation"

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Detailed measurement methodology
- ‚ùå Complete implementation plan
- ‚ùå Guaranteed achievability

---

### 3. Stakeholder Mapping ‚úì

- [ ] **Key stakeholders identified**
  - Decision makers named and role clarified
  - Implementers/executors identified
  - Affected groups identified (internal and external)
  - Internal champions and resistors noted

- [ ] **Stakeholder positions understood**
  - Key stakeholder priorities captured
  - Potential conflicts or misalignments identified
  - Power/influence dynamics noted
  - Communication preferences understood (where possible)

**What This Looks Like:**
- CEO (Decision): Wants proven ROI and quick wins
- VP Sales (Implementer): Concerned about customer messaging
- Customer Advisory Board (Affected): Wants faster response time
- Board of Directors (Decision): Wants clear competitive advantage

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Detailed influence analysis
- ‚ùå Change management plan
- ‚ùå Complete stakeholder mapping (just key stakeholders)

---

### 4. Analytical Foundation ‚úì

- [ ] **Initial data/analysis gathered**
  - Relevant historical data reviewed
  - Current performance data collected
  - Market context researched (high-level)
  - Preliminary competitive landscape sketch created

- [ ] **Analysis questions framed**
  - Key analytical questions for next phases defined
  - Data gaps identified
  - Assumptions about root causes listed
  - Investigation priorities established

- [ ] **Key assumptions documented**
  - Critical business assumptions captured
  - Market assumptions noted
  - Operational assumptions listed
  - Risk/uncertainty factors identified

**What This Looks Like:**
- Key Questions:
  - "Why are we losing these specific customers?"
  - "What do competitors offer that we don't?"
  - "What's our sustainable competitive advantage?"
- Data Gaps:
  - "Need lost customer exit interviews"
  - "Need detailed competitive pricing analysis"
  - "Need market research on customer preferences"

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Complete data gathering
- ‚ùå Deep analysis
- ‚ùå Hypothesis testing
- ‚ùå Comprehensive market research

---

### 5. Documentation & Handoff ‚úì

- [ ] **Strategic Brief created and finalized**
  - Executive summary of findings
  - Problem statement (clear and quantified)
  - Business impact articulated
  - Success criteria stated
  - Key stakeholders listed
  - Assumptions documented

- [ ] **Persona Handoff document created**
  - What DEFINE discovered summarized
  - Key findings from this phase
  - Strategic Specialist questions for next phase
  - Any decisions made during DEFINE
  - Data/resources available for SPLIT phase
  - Risk considerations noted

- [ ] **All work products organized**
  - Analysis work documented
  - Data sources referenced
  - Preliminary findings captured
  - Research artifacts linked
  - Documentation accessible to next persona

**What This Looks Like:**
- Strategic Brief: 2-3 page document with problem, context, impact, success criteria
- Handoff Doc: 1-2 page transition document highlighting key insights and questions
- Supporting Materials: Raw data, research notes, stakeholder interviews

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Polished presentation
- ‚ùå Full competitor analysis
- ‚ùå Complete market data
- ‚ùå Implementation recommendations

---

## Enhancing Criteria (Improving Quality)

These items strengthen the phase but aren't strictly blocking:

- [ ] **Context brief includes scenario considerations**
  - Best case scenario sketched
  - Worst case scenario sketched
  - Most likely scenario articulated

- [ ] **Preliminary insights identified**
  - Preliminary patterns noted
  - Initial hypotheses about root causes formed
  - Competitive positioning first thoughts captured

- [ ] **Stakeholder priorities hierarchy**
  - Stakeholder priorities ranked by importance
  - Potential win-win opportunities identified
  - Known trade-offs surfaced

- [ ] **Financial framework outlined**
  - Potential economic model sketched
  - Cost/benefit framework identified
  - Investment requirements estimated (order of magnitude)

- [ ] **Risk/constraint analysis initiated**
  - Regulatory or legal constraints identified
  - Technical constraints noted
  - Resource constraints identified
  - Time constraints understood

---

## Quality Checks (Before Handoff)

Before confirming phase completion, ask yourself:

1. **Can the Strategic Specialist productively decompose this problem?**
   - Is the problem clear enough to break down?
   - Are boundaries defined?
   - Would more clarity help or would it emerge during decomposition?

2. **Will the Specialist know what questions to investigate?**
   - Are analytical questions clearly framed?
   - Are data gaps identified?
   - Are assumptions explicit?

3. **Can we measure success when we're done?**
   - Are metrics specific enough?
   - Are targets clear?
   - Can we track progress?

4. **Does the user feel confident about the problem definition?**
   - Have they confirmed their own clarity?
   - Do they feel heard and understood?
   - Are they ready to move forward?

---

## Readiness Assessment

### ‚úÖ Ready to Proceed to SPLIT When

All blocking criteria are met:
- Problem is clear, quantified, and bounded
- Success criteria are defined and measurable
- Key stakeholders are identified
- Analytical foundation is established
- Documentation is complete and handed off

**The Specialist will have sufficient foundation to decompose the problem effectively.**

---

### üîÑ Needs More Work When

One or more blocking criteria are unmet:

- **Problem still unclear?**
  - ‚Üí Spend more time on problem articulation
  - ‚Üí Interview additional stakeholders
  - ‚Üí Refine scope boundaries

- **Impact not quantified?**
  - ‚Üí Gather more financial data
  - ‚Üí Define business metrics
  - ‚Üí Establish baseline measurements

- **Success criteria vague?**
  - ‚Üí Define specific, measurable targets
  - ‚Üí Get stakeholder agreement on metrics
  - ‚Üí Clarify trade-offs between criteria

- **Stakeholders not understood?**
  - ‚Üí Map power/interest/influence dynamics
  - ‚Üí Interview key stakeholders
  - ‚Üí Identify alignment/conflict areas

---

## What This Phase DOES Include

‚úÖ Clear problem statement
‚úÖ Business impact quantification
‚úÖ Success criteria definition
‚úÖ Stakeholder identification
‚úÖ Analytical foundation
‚úÖ Key assumptions documented
‚úÖ Strategic brief prepared

---

## What This Phase DOES NOT Include

‚ùå Root cause analysis (that's SPLIT/ANALYSE)
‚ùå Detailed market research (that's ANALYSE)
‚ùå Competitive analysis (that's ANALYSE)
‚ùå Solution recommendations (that's DECIDE/ACT)
‚ùå Implementation planning (that's ACT)
‚ùå Change management strategy (that's STORY/ACT)

---

## Common Blockers & How to Resolve

| Blocker | Signal | Resolution |
|---------|--------|-----------|
| **Problem too vague** | "It's complicated" | Use problem-structuring task to clarify |
| **Impact unmeasured** | No numbers mentioned | Gather baseline data and financial impact |
| **Scope too large** | Affects everything | Narrow to specific area; plan phased approach |
| **Stakeholders misaligned** | Conflicting views | Interview each stakeholder separately; document |
| **Success undefined** | "We'll know it when we see it" | Define specific, measurable metrics |
| **Data unavailable** | "We don't have that" | Identify what IS available; proceed with assumptions |

---

## Post-Completion Actions

Once this checklist passes:

1. **Create Persona Handoff Document**
   - Use `persona-handoff-template.md`
   - Summarize findings
   - Highlight questions for Specialist

2. **Prepare Strategic Brief**
   - Use `strategic-brief.md` template
   - Document problem, context, impact
   - Include success criteria and stakeholders

3. **Hand off to Strategic Specialist**
   - Share Strategic Brief
   - Share Persona Handoff
   - Confirm Specialist ready to proceed
   - Load SPLIT phase files

4. **Archive DEFINE Materials**
   - Save all analysis work
   - Reference for future phases
   - Keep accessible (may need to revisit)

---

## Notes & Observations

Use this space to capture phase-specific insights:

- **What worked well in this phase?**

- **What was challenging?**

- **Unexpected insights?**

- **For future engagements:**

---

## Sign-Off

**Phase Completed By:** __________________ (Persona)

**Date Completed:** __________________

**Confirmed Ready for SPLIT:** ‚òê Yes ‚òê No

**If No, specific blockers:**

---

## Related Resources

- **Task:** `tasks/problem-structuring.md`
- **Task:** `tasks/context-assessment-framework.md`
- **Task:** `tasks/business-intelligence-analysis.md`
- **Framework Reference:** `data/00_strategic-frameworks.md` (Define section)
- **Output Template:** `templates/strategic-brief.md`
- **Handoff Template:** `templates/persona-handoff-template.md`

==================== END: define-phase-completion-checklist ====================

==================== START: execution-planning-quality-checklist ====================
# Execution Planning Quality Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that execution plans are detailed, sequenced logically, have clear ownership, and are realistic for implementation. Ensure plans can successfully guide execution from start to finish.

## What Gets Validated

**Task Reference:** `tasks/execution-planning.md`

**Used In:** ACT phase for translating strategy to action

**Audience:** Execution leaders, project managers, team leads

---

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. Plan Has Clear Objectives & Success Criteria ‚úì

- [ ] **What success looks like is defined**
  - What are we trying to achieve?
  - What's the end goal?
  - How will we measure success?
  - What's done/acceptable?

- [ ] **Success metrics are specific**
  - Financial metrics (revenue, profitability)?
  - Operational metrics (customers, velocity)?
  - Quality metrics (satisfaction, churn)?
  - Timeline metrics (deadline)?

- [ ] **Objectives are aligned with strategy**
  - Do plan objectives match strategic decision?
  - Are we moving toward the goal?
  - Are we solving the right problem?
  - Does execution serve strategy?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
OBJECTIVES & SUCCESS CRITERIA:

Strategic Decision: Launch SMB product offering

Plan Objective:
Deliver viable SMB product to market and establish market foothold
with 10+ customers in first 12 months.

Success Criteria:

Financial Metrics:
- $500K+ ARR by Month 12 (revenue target)
- Gross margin 75%+ (profitability target)
- Customer CAC <$50K (efficiency target)

Operational Metrics:
- 10+ customers by Month 12 (adoption target)
- <45 day implementation (speed target)
- 3+ product releases (velocity target)

Quality Metrics:
- Customer NPS 50+ (satisfaction target)
- <8% churn (retention target)
- 95%+ uptime (reliability target)

Timeline:
- MVP ready Month 6 (product target)
- Pilot customers live Month 8 (validation target)
- Market launch Month 10 (launch target)
- Target profitability Month 18 (financial target)

Overall Success Definition:
Product is viable (NPS 50+), adopted (10+ customers),
efficient (CAC <$50K), and on path to profitability.
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect metrics
- ‚ùå Quantified for every goal
- ‚ùå Unanimous agreement
- ‚ùå Static (will evolve)

---

### 2. Plan Has Detailed Sequence & Milestones ‚úì

- [ ] **Work is sequenced logically**
  - Do tasks happen in right order?
  - Are dependencies clear?
  - Would someone know what to do?
  - Are critical path items identified?

- [ ] **Milestones are meaningful**
  - What are the key checkpoints?
  - When does each milestone occur?
  - What indicates milestone completion?
  - Are milestones realistic?

- [ ] **Timeline is realistic**
  - Is 18-month plan credible?
  - Are effort estimates reasonable?
  - Is schedule achievable?
  - What are the risks to timeline?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
EXECUTION PLAN SEQUENCE:

Phase 1: Foundation (Month 1-2)
- Hire product lead for SMB (critical path)
- Define SMB product scope (depends on lead hire)
- Build development team (parallel to scope)
- Establish SMB GTM strategy (parallel)
Milestone: Team in place; scope locked

Phase 2: Development (Month 3-6)
- Build core product features (critical path)
- Develop implementation playbook (parallel)
- Establish support process (parallel)
- Conduct 3 pilot customer interviews (parallel)
Milestone: MVP ready for pilot testing

Phase 3: Pilot (Month 7-9)
- Recruit 3-5 pilot customers (depends on product ready)
- Implement with pilots (depends on product ready)
- Gather feedback; refine product (depends on implementation)
- Train sales team (parallel)
Milestone: Pilots live; feedback gathered

Phase 4: Launch (Month 10-12)
- Finalize product based on pilot learning (depends on pilot feedback)
- Launch market GTM campaign (depends on product ready)
- Acquire first customers (depends on GTM launch)
- Measure results; optimize (parallel)
Milestone: 5-10 customers acquired; $500K ARR on track

Phase 5: Scale (Month 13-18)
- Acquire additional customers (depends on GTM working)
- Build customer success function (depends on customer growth)
- Optimize product based on customer feedback (parallel)
- Prepare for profitability (parallel)
Milestone: 10+ customers; on track to profitability

Critical Path:
Product lead hire ‚Üí Product scope ‚Üí Development ‚Üí MVP ‚Üí
Pilot feedback ‚Üí Product refinement ‚Üí Launch ‚Üí Customer acquisition
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Gantt chart with all details
- ‚ùå Week-by-week breakdown
- ‚ùå Perfect timeline accuracy
- ‚ùå Zero dependency management

---

### 3. Plan Has Clear Ownership & Accountability ‚úì

- [ ] **Owner assigned to each major workstream**
  - Product owner: Accountable for product
  - GTM owner: Accountable for sales/marketing
  - Operations owner: Accountable for support/systems
  - Executive sponsor: Accountable for overall execution

- [ ] **Roles & responsibilities are clear**
  - What is each person accountable for?
  - Who makes decisions in each area?
  - Who reports progress?
  - Who has authority to make changes?

- [ ] **Decision rights are clear**
  - Who decides when things change?
  - Who escalates issues?
  - Who commits resources?
  - Who decides go/no-go?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
OWNERSHIP & ACCOUNTABILITY:

Product Workstream:
- Owner: VP Product (hired new, SMB expert)
- Accountability: Product ready by Month 6; NPS 50+ by Month 12
- Team: 1 PM + 3-4 engineers + 1 QA
- Decisions: Feature prioritization, architecture, tradeoffs
- Reporting: Weekly to Executive Sponsor

GTM Workstream:
- Owner: VP Sales (expanded role from enterprise)
- Accountability: 10+ customers by Month 12; CAC <$50K
- Team: 1 Account executive + 1 Sales development + marketing
- Decisions: Customer targeting, pricing, partnership
- Reporting: Weekly to Executive Sponsor

Operations Workstream:
- Owner: VP Customer Success (new function)
- Accountability: Implementation <45 days; churn <8%; NPS 50+
- Team: 1 Customer success manager + 1 Support person
- Decisions: Process, tools, customer success approach
- Reporting: Weekly to Executive Sponsor

Executive Sponsor:
- Owner: Chief Product Officer
- Accountability: Overall execution; timeline; budget
- Authority: Remove blockers; adjust resources; make escalation calls
- Reporting: Monthly to CEO; quarterly to Board

Decision Rights:
- Feature changes: VP Product (under budget constraints)
- Customer changes: VP Sales (with VP Product input)
- Process changes: VP CS (with support from ops)
- Budget/resource changes: CFO (with Executive Sponsor approval)
- Strategic pivots: CEO (with Executive Sponsor recommendation)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Detailed org chart
- ‚ùå Full RACI matrix
- ‚ùå Extensive governance structure
- ‚ùå Unanimous ownership clarity

---

### 4. Plan Has Resource Allocation & Budget ‚úì

- [ ] **Headcount is allocated**
  - How many people needed?
  - What skills/roles required?
  - When are they needed?
  - Are people available?

- [ ] **Budget is allocated**
  - How much capital needed?
  - Breakdown by category (salaries, tools, marketing)?
  - When is capital needed?
  - Is budget approved?

- [ ] **Resources vs. Plan are aligned**
  - Does team size match scope?
  - Does budget match timeline?
  - Are resources sufficient?
  - Are there bottlenecks?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
RESOURCE ALLOCATION:

Headcount Plan:

Product Team (leads Month 3):
- 1 VP Product (hired by Month 1) - $200K salary
- 1 Product Manager (hired Month 2) - $150K salary
- 3-4 Engineers (hired by Month 3) - $150K each = $450-600K
- 1 QA Engineer (hired Month 3) - $120K
- Total Product: 6-7 people; $920K-1.07M annual

GTM Team (leads Month 5):
- 1 Account Executive (from enterprise team) - $150K
- 1 Sales Development Rep (new hire Month 4) - $80K
- 1 Marketing Manager (part-time from enterprise) - $60K allocation
- Total GTM: 2.5 people; $290K annual allocation

Operations Team (leads Month 7):
- 1 VP Customer Success (new hire Month 6) - $150K
- 1 Customer Success Manager (hired Month 8) - $100K
- 1 Support person (part-time Month 8, full-time Month 10) - $60K
- Total Ops: 2.5 people; $310K annual allocation

Total Headcount: 10-12 FTE equivalent
Total Annual Salary Cost: $1.52M

Budget Allocation:

Personnel: $1.52M (70%)
Tools & Infrastructure: $200K (10%)
- AWS/hosting
- SaaS tools (CRM, analytics, etc.)
- Development tools

Marketing & Customer Acquisition: $300K (15%)
- Campaign spend
- Events
- Content

Contingency: $100K (5%)

Total Annual Budget: $2.12M

Timeline of Investment:
Month 1-2: $400K (hiring; foundation)
Month 3-6: $800K (development; team ramp)
Month 7-9: $600K (pilot; GTM prep)
Month 10-12: $320K (launch; early customers)

Total 12-month investment: $2.12M
(Note: Year 2 would be similar plus scaling investments)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect headcount estimates
- ‚ùå Detailed budget breakdowns
- ‚ùå Fully approved budgets
- ‚ùå Zero overruns (contingency included)

---

### 5. Plan Identifies & Addresses Key Risks ‚úì

- [ ] **Major risks are identified**
  - What could derail execution?
  - What's the biggest risk?
  - What external factors could impact?
  - Are obvious risks included?

- [ ] **Risk mitigation is outlined**
  - How would we prevent key risks?
  - How would we detect early?
  - How would we respond?
  - Is mitigation realistic?

- [ ] **Contingency plans exist**
  - If timeline slips, what do we do?
  - If customer adoption slower, what do we do?
  - If team member leaves, what do we do?
  - Are alternatives identified?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
RISK MANAGEMENT:

Risk 1: Product Development Timeline Slips

Risk: Development takes longer than 6 months

Mitigation:
- Hire experienced VP Product (knows how to execute fast)
- Reduce scope to must-haves only
- Weekly milestone tracking
- Resource contingency built in

Detection:
- Monthly milestone reviews (Is product on track?)
- If 2+ weeks behind, escalate
- Trigger: Month 4 milestone slipped

Response:
- Reduce scope further (cut lower-priority features)
- Add resources if available
- Delay launch 2-4 weeks (manage expectations)
- Descope 2-3 features to stay close to timeline

Residual risk: Acceptable (could live with Month 8 launch)

---

Risk 2: Pilot Customers Don't Adopt/Churn

Risk: Pilots show low satisfaction (NPS <40) or churn

Mitigation:
- Carefully select pilot customers (strong fit)
- Dedicated support during pilot
- Weekly check-ins with pilots
- Rapid iteration based on feedback

Detection:
- Monthly pilot satisfaction tracking
- NPS target Month 8: 50+
- If NPS <40, pause additional pilots

Response:
- Pause new customer acquisitions
- Focus on pilot customer success
- Product refinement based on feedback
- 4-week re-engagement effort
- If still <40 NPS after refinement, reconsider market fit

Residual risk: Acceptable (market could be wrong; would pivot)

---

Risk 3: Key Talent Leaves

Risk: VP Product or key engineer departs mid-project

Mitigation:
- Competitive compensation (top-of-market pay)
- Clear equity/incentives for retention
- Strong vision/mission (people motivated)
- Succession plan in place

Detection:
- Regular 1:1s with key people
- Manager check-ins on engagement
- Pulse surveys quarterly

Response:
- Emergency backfill (recruitment)
- Interim coverage (other team members)
- Compressed timeline (if necessary)
- Scope adjustment (if necessary)

Residual risk: Manageable (could impact timeline; not fatal)

---

Risk 4: Faster Competitor Response

Risk: Competitor launches SMB product Month 8 (before us)

Mitigation:
- Move fast (hit Month 10 launch target)
- Differentiate via vertical expertise
- Build customer relationships early (pilots become advocates)
- Lock in early customers (incentivize commitment)

Detection:
- Weekly competitive intelligence
- If competitor announces, assess threat
- Re-evaluate positioning if needed

Response:
- Accelerate differentiation (enhance vertical focus)
- Emphasize customer success (switching cost)
- Consider partnership/acquisition (if strategic fit)

Residual risk: Acceptable (18-month lead is still defensible)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Exhaustive risk list
- ‚ùå Perfect risk mitigation
- ‚ùå Zero contingency
- ‚ùå Risk-free execution

---

### 6. Plan Includes Communication & Governance ‚úì

- [ ] **Stakeholder communication is planned**
  - Who needs updates?
  - How frequently?
  - What format?
  - What's the escalation path?

- [ ] **Progress tracking is defined**
  - How will we measure progress?
  - What metrics matter?
  - How frequently reviewed?
  - Who tracks and reports?

- [ ] **Decision governance is clear**
  - How are go/no-go decisions made?
  - When do we assess progress?
  - Who has authority?
  - What's the escalation process?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
COMMUNICATION & GOVERNANCE:

Stakeholder Communication:

Executive Sponsor (CPO):
- Frequency: Weekly
- Format: 30-min status meeting
- Topics: Milestones, risks, decisions needed
- Owner: Workstream leads rotate

Board:
- Frequency: Quarterly
- Format: 15-min board update
- Topics: Progress, key milestones, financials
- Owner: Executive Sponsor

Team:
- Frequency: Weekly
- Format: 1-hour all-hands meeting
- Topics: Progress, blockers, celebrations
- Owner: Executive Sponsor

Progress Tracking:

Weekly Metrics:
- Product: Feature completion %, bugs, velocity
- GTM: Pipeline, customer interest
- Ops: Support ticket volume, response time

Monthly Metrics:
- Product: Milestone achievement, team morale
- GTM: Conversation rate, deal pipeline
- Ops: Implementation time, customer NPS

Quarterly Metrics:
- Financial: Budget vs. actual, ARR trajectory
- Operational: Customer count, churn, retention
- Strategic: Competitive positioning, market feedback

Governance:

Monthly Executive Review:
- Review progress vs. plan
- Assess financials
- Review key risks
- Make go/no-go decisions
- Adjust plan if needed

Quarterly Board Review:
- High-level progress update
- Financial performance
- Key risks and mitigation
- Forward guidance

Go/No-Go Decision Points:
- Month 6: Product ready for pilot? (GO/NO-GO)
- Month 9: Pilot results positive? (GO/NO-GO)
- Month 12: Customer acquisition on track? (GO/NO-GO)
- Month 18: Profitability path clear? (GO/NO-GO)

Escalation Process:
- Issue identified by workstream lead
- Escalated to Executive Sponsor if can't resolve
- Executive Sponsor brings to monthly review
- If major: CEO and board notified
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect communication cadence
- ‚ùå Formal governance structure
- ‚ùå Multi-tier reporting
- ‚ùå Real-time dashboards

---

## Enhancing Criteria (Improving Quality)

These items strengthen the plan but aren't strictly blocking:

- [ ] **Detailed phase plans**
  - Does each phase have detailed plan?
  - Are activities broken down?
  - Are dependencies clear?

- [ ] **Change management approach**
  - How will we handle scope changes?
  - What's the approval process?
  - How will we manage expectations?

- [ ] **Dependency management**
  - Are external dependencies clear?
  - Supplier dependencies?
  - Customer dependencies?

- [ ] **Success criteria at each phase**
  - Phase 1: How do we know it was successful?
  - Phase 2: Same
  - Phase 3-5: Same

---

## Quality Checks (Before Approving)

Before confirming plan is complete, ask yourself:

1. **Is plan understandable?**
   - Could someone execute from this plan?
   - Are tasks and dependencies clear?
   - Would execution team know what to do?

2. **Is plan realistic?**
   - Are estimates reasonable?
   - Is timeline credible?
   - Is team sized right?
   - Are risks acknowledged?

3. **Does plan align with strategy?**
   - Are plan objectives aligned with decision?
   - Does execution serve the goal?
   - Would success achieve the outcome?

4. **Are we ready to execute?**
   - Are resources committed?
   - Is budget approved?
   - Is team in place?
   - Are we ready to start?

---

## Readiness Assessment

### ‚úÖ Plan is Ready When

All blocking criteria are met:
- Clear objectives and success criteria
- Detailed sequence and milestones
- Clear ownership and accountability
- Resource allocation and budget
- Key risks identified and addressed
- Communication and governance planned

**Plan can be handed to execution team; execution can begin.**

---

### üîÑ Plan Needs More Work When

- **Objectives unclear?** ‚Üí Define what success looks like
- **Sequence confusing?** ‚Üí Map dependencies; clarify sequence
- **Ownership missing?** ‚Üí Assign clear owners
- **Budget unclear?** ‚Üí Estimate resources; allocate budget
- **Risks ignored?** ‚Üí Identify and plan mitigation
- **No governance?** ‚Üí Define decision and communication process

---

## Post-Validation Actions

Once this checklist passes:

1. **Get Executive Approval**
   - Present plan to leadership
   - Address questions/concerns
   - Confirm resource commitments
   - Authorize execution

2. **Prepare Execution Team**
   - Share plan with full team
   - Clarify roles and responsibilities
   - Confirm understanding
   - Answer questions

3. **Set Up Governance**
   - Schedule regular reviews
   - Create progress tracking system
   - Establish communication cadence
   - Prepare materials/templates

4. **Begin Execution**
   - Month 1 activities start
   - Progress tracking begins
   - Regular governance meetings start
   - Execution underway

---

# Final Synthesis Validation Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that final synthesis consolidates complete strategic work, documents all decisions, and captures learning for organizational knowledge and future reference.

## What Gets Validated

**Template Reference:** `templates/final-synthesis-template.md`

**Used In:** After ACT phase (project completion)

**Audience:** Executive team, knowledge management, future projects

---

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. Complete Project Summary Is Documented ‚úì

- [ ] **All 7 phases are summarized**
  - DEFINE: Problem and context
  - SPLIT: Problem decomposition
  - ANALYSE: Data analysis
  - INSIGHT: Insights and opportunities
  - STORY: Strategic narrative
  - DECIDE: Decision and recommendation
  - ACT: Implementation and execution

- [ ] **Project outcome is clear**
  - What decision was made?
  - What was recommended?
  - What was executed?
  - What was the result?

- [ ] **Key milestones are documented**
  - Major decision points noted
  - Timeline of execution
  - Key transitions marked
  - Completion date clear

**What This Looks Like:**

```
PROJECT SUMMARY:

DEFINE Phase:
Problem: SMB market gap created by enterprise positioning
Context: Competitors entering space; revenue at risk; opportunity exists
Outcome: Clear problem definition; scope boundaries set

SPLIT Phase:
Problem Decomposition: Root causes identified (strategic positioning)
Hypotheses: Market gap is fixable via vertical strategy
Outcome: Clear hypothesis for testing

ANALYSE Phase:
Market Data: $693M SAM; $122M SOM; competitors identified
Financial: Unit economics strong; profitability path clear
Outcome: Financial model supports strategy

INSIGHT Phase:
Competitive Positioning: Vertical expertise is differentiator
Business Model: Separate SMB product with premium pricing
Outcome: Clear strategy for market entry

STORY Phase:
Strategic Narrative: "Vertical expertise for focused markets"
Messaging: Built for [vertical], by experts, fast to implement
Outcome: Clear brand positioning

DECIDE Phase:
Recommendation: Proceed with vertical SMB strategy
Decision: Approved (CEO + Board)
Plan: $3.5M investment; Month 6 MVP; Month 12 launch
Outcome: Executive commitment; funding approved

ACT Phase:
Execution: Hired VP Product; team assembled; development started
Milestones: MVP Month 6; Pilot Month 9; Launch Month 12
Outcome: Project now in execution; tracking to plan

---

Project Outcome Summary:
Strategic question: Should we enter SMB market?
Answer: YES, via vertical-focused strategy
Investment: $3.5M capital approved
Expected return: $3M+ SMB revenue by Year 3
Timeline: 18-month execution plan

Timeline:
- Month 0-1: Project initiation and team assembly
- Month 1-6: Strategy development phases
- Month 6-9: Pilot phase
- Month 9-12: Market launch
- Month 12-18: Scale phase
- Project completion: Month 18 (in progress)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Exhaustive phase documentation
- ‚ùå All deliverables detailed
- ‚ùå Perfect summary completeness
- ‚ùå Novel insights (recap is sufficient)

---

### 2. All Strategic Findings Are Consolidated ‚úì

- [ ] **Major findings from all phases collected**
  - Problem definition findings
  - Root cause findings
  - Market findings
  - Competitive findings
  - Financial findings
  - Risk findings

- [ ] **Findings are organized for reference**
  - Logical organization
  - Easy to find specific finding
  - Connected to source phase
  - Evidence noted

- [ ] **Confidence levels are clear**
  - Which findings are high confidence?
  - Which are medium/low confidence?
  - What was validation method?
  - What remains uncertain?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
CONSOLIDATED FINDINGS:

High Confidence Findings:
1. Strategic positioning created market gap
   Evidence: Customer interviews; competitive analysis; market trends
   Confidence: HIGH
   Implication: Gap is addressable

2. Vertical expertise can create competitive advantage
   Evidence: Competitive benchmarking; customer interviews
   Confidence: MEDIUM-HIGH
   Implication: Defensible positioning exists

3. Unit economics are strong
   Evidence: Financial modeling; comparable companies
   Confidence: MEDIUM-HIGH
   Implication: Business is viable

Medium Confidence Findings:
4. Customer will adopt from startup
   Evidence: Pilot results; customer willingness
   Confidence: MEDIUM
   Implication: Market adoption achievable but not certain

5. Competitors won't match quickly
   Evidence: Competitive capability analysis
   Confidence: MEDIUM
   Implication: Window exists but timing uncertain

Low Confidence/Assumptions:
6. Can execute 6-month product development
   Evidence: Comparable company timelines; internal estimates
   Confidence: LOW-MEDIUM (depends on execution)
   Implication: Product timeline is critical path

7. Customer acquisition will match model
   Evidence: Industry benchmarks; internal projections
   Confidence: LOW-MEDIUM (depends on GTM execution)
   Implication: Profitability depends on CAC control
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Every finding detailed
- ‚ùå Perfect confidence scoring
- ‚ùå All supporting data
- ‚ùå Exhaustive evidence

---

### 3. All Decisions Are Documented ‚úì

- [ ] **Major decisions are recorded**
  - What decision was made?
  - When was it made?
  - Who made it?
  - What was the rationale?

- [ ] **Decision trade-offs are clear**
  - What did we gain?
  - What did we give up?
  - Were alternatives considered?
  - Why this choice?

- [ ] **Decision implications are noted**
  - How did decision shape strategy?
  - What constraints did it create?
  - What opportunities did it enable?
  - How would changing decision impact plan?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
STRATEGIC DECISIONS DOCUMENTED:

Decision 1: Pursue SMB Market Entry
Timeline: Month 3 (ANALYSE phase)
Maker: CEO + Strategic Team
Rationale: Market gap exists; defensible strategy possible; financial viability clear
Alternatives: (1) Stay enterprise-only [rejected]; (2) Aggressive pricing strategy [rejected]
Trade-off: Organizational complexity for market opportunity
Status: APPROVED and EXECUTED

Decision 2: Use Vertical Focusing Strategy
Timeline: Month 4 (INSIGHT phase)
Maker: CEO + Product Leadership
Rationale: Vertical expertise creates defensible moat; premium pricing justified
Alternatives: (1) Horizontal SMB [rejected - too competitive]; (2) Partnership [rejected - lose control]
Trade-off: Narrower market initially for stronger positioning
Status: APPROVED and EXECUTED

Decision 3: Invest $3.5M Capital
Timeline: Month 6 (DECIDE phase)
Maker: CEO + Board
Rationale: Financial model supports ROI; break-even Year 3; profitability Year 4
Alternatives: (1) Lower investment [rejected - insufficient]; (2) Partnerships [rejected - dilutes strategy]
Trade-off: Capital commitment for growth opportunity
Status: APPROVED and COMMITTED

Decision 4: Build Separate Product (vs. Embedded)
Timeline: Month 5 (INSIGHT phase)
Maker: Product Leadership
Rationale: Separate product allows vertical focus; clear brand; independent roadmap
Alternatives: (1) Integrated into enterprise [rejected - brand confusion]
Trade-off: Engineering complexity for strategic clarity
Status: APPROVED and IN EXECUTION

Decision Impact Assessment:
- If Decision 1 reversed: Stay enterprise-only; miss SMB opportunity
- If Decision 2 reversed: Generic SMB approach; low differentiation
- If Decision 3 reversed: Insufficient resources; can't execute
- If Decision 4 reversed: Conflicted priorities; brand confusion
All decisions are critical to strategy; reversal would be major pivot.
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Every decision documented
- ‚ùå Perfect alternative analysis
- ‚ùå Exhaustive implications
- ‚ùå Immutable decisions

---

### 4. Implementation Plan Is Finalized ‚úì

- [ ] **Execution plan is documented**
  - What will be executed?
  - Timeline for execution
  - Ownership and accountability
  - Resource commitments

- [ ] **Success metrics are defined**
  - What's the measure of success?
  - What are financial targets?
  - What are operational targets?
  - What's timeline for assessment?

- [ ] **Contingency plans exist**
  - If adoption slower: what's plan B?
  - If profitability delayed: what's plan B?
  - If market rejects: what's plan B?
  - Are alternatives identified?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
IMPLEMENTATION PLAN SUMMARY:

Execution Overview:
Phase 1 (Month 1-2): Foundation
- Team assembly (VP Product, engineering, sales)
- Product scope definition
- GTM strategy development

Phase 2 (Month 3-6): Development
- SMB product MVP development
- Pilot customer recruitment
- Sales enablement

Phase 3 (Month 7-9): Pilot
- Implement with 3-5 pilot customers
- Gather feedback; refine
- Train sales team

Phase 4 (Month 10-12): Launch
- Market launch campaign
- Customer acquisition
- $500K ARR target

Phase 5 (Month 13-18): Scale
- Expand to 10+ customers
- Establish profitability path
- Prepare for Year 2 expansion

---

Success Metrics:

Financial:
- Year 1: $500K+ ARR (10+ customers at $50K+ ACV)
- Year 2: $1.5M+ ARR (path to profitability)
- Year 3: $3M+ ARR (profitability achieved)

Operational:
- Customer NPS: 50+ (satisfaction target)
- Customer churn: <8% annual (retention target)
- Implementation time: <45 days (speed target)

Contingency Plans:

If Customer Adoption Slower:
- Action: Extend timeline; adjust targets
- Go/No-Go: Month 12 decision point
- Trigger: <5 customers acquired
- Alternative: Pivot to adjacent vertical

If Profitability Delayed:
- Action: Extend investment timeline
- Go/No-Go: Month 18 decision point
- Trigger: Revenue <$1.5M or churn >8%
- Alternative: Merge with enterprise; consolidate products

If Market Rejects Strategy:
- Action: Customer research; rapid iteration
- Go/No-Go: Month 9 decision point
- Trigger: NPS <40 or <3 pilots completed
- Alternative: Pivot to different positioning or model
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Detailed project plans
- ‚ùå Every contingency documented
- ‚ùå Perfect execution details
- ‚ùå Risk-free plan

---

### 5. Learning & Insights Are Captured ‚úì

- [ ] **What we learned is documented**
  - What surprised us?
  - What changed our thinking?
  - What would we do differently?
  - What should future projects know?

- [ ] **Effective approaches are noted**
  - What methodology worked well?
  - What approach would we use again?
  - What was efficient?
  - What would we recommend to others?

- [ ] **Lessons for future projects**
  - General principles extracted
  - Context-specific learning noted
  - Transferable practices identified
  - Knowledge assets created

**What This Looks Like:**

```
LEARNING CAPTURE:

Key Learnings:

Learning 1: Vertical Focus Is Powerful Positioning Tool
Insight: Vertical positioning solved multiple problems (differentiation, pricing, GTM)
Why: Customers prefer specialists; specialists command premium pricing; specialists have defensible moats
Future application: Strongly recommend vertical focus for software companies
Impact: Changes how we think about market segmentation

Learning 2: Financial Models Need Grounding in Real Data
Insight: Our adoption curve assumptions were initially aggressive; customer validation was critical
Why: Industry benchmarks are general; our specific market could vary significantly
Future application: Always validate assumptions with real customer conversations
Impact: Better financial projections; more realistic planning

Learning 3: Persona-Based Handoffs Prevent Knowledge Loss
Insight: Structured handoffs between personas preserved context and insights
Why: Each persona brought different perspective; transfer was intentional
Future application: Use persona handoff approach for all strategic projects
Impact: Better knowledge management; faster phase transitions

Learning 4: Competitive Intelligence Must Be Continuous
Insight: Competitive landscape changed mid-project; continuous monitoring caught it
Why: Market moves fast; weekly monitoring is essential
Future application: Build competitive intelligence into ongoing governance
Impact: Better risk management; faster adaptation to threats

---

Effective Approaches:

Approach 1: Customer Interviews for Validation
What worked: Direct customer conversations validated assumptions better than market research
Effectiveness: HIGH (compelling evidence; authentic feedback)
Would use again: YES (every strategic project)

Approach 2: Scenario Planning for Risk Mitigation
What worked: Best/base/worst case scenarios prepared contingency thinking
Effectiveness: HIGH (prevented surprises; had plans ready)
Would use again: YES (especially for new market entry)

Approach 3: Cross-Phase Pattern Analysis
What worked: Mid-point synthesis identified patterns that informed strategy
Effectiveness: MEDIUM-HIGH (added rigor; caught inconsistencies)
Would use again: YES (for projects of similar scope)

---

Transferable Practices:

Practice 1: Weekly Status Meetings
Recommendation: Keep team aligned; identify blockers early
How: Executive sponsor + workstream leads; 30 min
Impact: Prevented surprises; kept project on track

Practice 2: Go/No-Go Decision Points
Recommendation: Define clear decision thresholds upfront
How: Define success criteria at each phase; decide to proceed, pivot, or stop
Impact: Clear accountability; reduced scope creep

Practice 3: Assumption Documentation
Recommendation: Surface assumptions; validate them systematically
How: List key assumptions; confidence levels; testing approach
Impact: Better risk management; reduced surprises
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Every learning captured
- ‚ùå Perfect insight articulation
- ‚ùå Exhaustive future recommendations
- ‚ùå Complete knowledge transfer

---

### 6. Final Synthesis Document Is Complete ‚úì

- [ ] **Document is comprehensive**
  - All 7 phases summarized?
  - All decisions documented?
  - All findings consolidated?
  - Learning captured?

- [ ] **Document is well-organized**
  - Executive summary included?
  - Supporting detail organized?
  - Easy to navigate?
  - Professional quality?

- [ ] **Document is archived appropriately**
  - Will be preserved for future reference?
  - Easy to find when needed?
  - Accessible to right people?
  - Version control clear?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
FINAL SYNTHESIS DOCUMENT STRUCTURE:

1. Executive Summary (2 pages)
   - Strategic question addressed
   - Recommendation made
   - Decision outcome
   - Investment and timeline
   - Next steps

2. Project Overview (1 page)
   - 7-phase methodology
   - Timeline and milestones
   - Team and governance
   - Key decision points

3. Strategic Findings (3-4 pages)
   - Consolidated findings by phase
   - Confidence levels
   - Evidence cited
   - Implications noted

4. Strategic Decisions (2-3 pages)
   - All major decisions documented
   - Rationale and alternatives
   - Trade-offs explicit
   - Decision status

5. Implementation Plan (2-3 pages)
   - Execution timeline
   - Team and accountability
   - Success metrics
   - Contingency plans

6. Learning & Insights (2-3 pages)
   - What we learned
   - Effective approaches
   - Transferable practices
   - Recommendations for future

7. Appendices (5-10 pages)
   - Supporting data and analysis
   - Financial models
   - Risk assessments
   - Additional reference materials

Archival Plan:
- Location: Project records system
- Filename: [Project Name]_Final_Synthesis_[Date]
- Access: Available to project team and future strategists
- Search: Tagged by topic, industry, methodology for discoverability
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Polished presentation
- ‚ùå Exhaustive appendices
- ‚ùå Perfect completeness
- ‚ùå Formal publication quality

---

## Quality Checks (Before Approving)

1. **Is project outcome clear?**
   - What was decided?
   - What was executed?
   - What was the result?

2. **Are key decisions documented?**
   - All major decisions included?
   - Rationale clear?
   - Could someone understand?

3. **Is learning captured?**
   - What did we learn?
   - What would we do differently?
   - What should future projects know?

4. **Is document useful for reference?**
   - Could someone use this later?
   - Would they understand context?
   - Could they apply learning?

---

## Readiness Assessment

### ‚úÖ Synthesis is Ready When

All blocking criteria are met:
- Complete project summary documented
- All strategic findings consolidated
- All decisions documented
- Implementation plan finalized
- Learning and insights captured
- Final document is complete and archived

**Project is complete; knowledge is preserved; learning is captured.**

==================== START: financial-model-validation-checklist ====================
# Financial Model Validation Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that a completed Financial Model provides credible financial projections and analysis to support strategic decision-making with clear assumptions, sound methodology, and transparent scenarios.

## What Gets Validated

**Template Reference:** `templates/financial-model.md`

**Used In:** ANALYSE and DECIDE phases for financial validation of strategic options

**Audience:** Finance leadership, CFO, executives evaluating financial viability of strategies

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. Model Scope & Structure ‚úì

- [ ] **Financial model scope is clear**
  - What's being modeled? (Revenue? Costs? Profit?)
  - What time period? (1 year? 3 years? 5 years?)
  - What level of detail? (Company level? Product level?)
  - What scenarios included?

- [ ] **Model structure is logical**
  - Is model organized in clear sections?
  - Are inputs separated from calculations?
  - Are outputs clearly marked?
  - Can someone understand model structure?

- [ ] **Model covers key financial metrics**
  - Revenue projections
  - Cost structure (COGS, OpEx)
  - Profitability (Gross Margin, EBITDA, Net Income)
  - Cash flow (if relevant)
  - Key metrics (CAC, LTV, payback period, ROI)

**What This Looks Like:**
```
MODEL SCOPE:
- Being modeled: Revenue and profitability for SMB offering
- Time period: 3-year plan (Year 1, 2, 3)
- Detail level: By product (SMB vs. Enterprise), by customer segment
- Scenarios: Base case, upside case, downside case

MODEL STRUCTURE:
INPUTS (Assumptions):
- Market size and adoption rate
- Customer acquisition cost
- Pricing per customer
- Customer lifetime value
- Team costs and expansion

CALCULATIONS:
- Revenue = Customers √ó Pricing
- Gross Margin = Revenue - COGS
- Operating Expense = Team + Marketing + Sales
- EBITDA = Gross Margin - OpEx
- Net Income = EBITDA - Other costs

OUTPUTS:
- Revenue projection (3-year)
- Profitability by year
- Payback period
- 5-year NPV
- Key metrics by scenario

SCENARIOS:
- Base case (most likely assumptions)
- Upside case (optimistic assumptions)
- Downside case (conservative assumptions)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect model elegance
- ‚ùå Every possible metric
- ‚ùå 10-year projections (3 years typical)
- ‚ùå Daily/weekly cashflow detail

---

### 2. Key Assumptions Are Documented ‚úì

- [ ] **All critical assumptions stated**
  - What are we assuming about market?
  - What are we assuming about costs?
  - What are we assuming about growth?
  - What are we assuming about operations?

- [ ] **Assumptions are realistic**
  - Are they based on data?
  - Are they benchmarked to industry/competitors?
  - Are they validated with stakeholders?
  - Would someone believe these assumptions?

- [ ] **Assumption sensitivity is addressed**
  - Which assumptions have most impact on outcome?
  - What happens if key assumptions are wrong?
  - How sensitive is model to each key variable?
  - What would we need to be wrong about?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
KEY ASSUMPTIONS:

MARKET ASSUMPTIONS:
- SMB market size: $2B (validated by market research)
- Market growth rate: 25% annually (benchmarked to industry)
- Our market capture: 2% by Year 3 (based on competitive positioning)
- Basis: Conservative relative to TAM; market research suggests 3-4%

CUSTOMER ASSUMPTIONS:
- Customer acquisition cost (CAC): $5K (based on sales team estimates)
- Basis: SMB AE handles 3-4 deals/month at $15K avg deal; ~$5K CAC
- Confidence: MODERATE (varies by channel; average across channels)

- Customer lifetime value (LTV): $60K (3 year relationship, $20K/year)
- Basis: Pilot customer data; enterprise customers similar profile
- Confidence: MODERATE (SMB retention may differ; need validation)

- CAC payback period: 18 months (acceptable for SaaS)
- Basis: Industry standard; our enterprise is 12 months
- Confidence: MODERATE (higher than enterprise due to SMB support needs)

COST ASSUMPTIONS:
- Team ramp: 5 people Year 1; 10 by Year 2; 15 by Year 3
- Cost per person: $150K average (blended salary + benefits)
- Basis: Our current team costs; adjusted for SMB roles
- Confidence: HIGH (comparable to enterprise team)

- Gross margin: 75% (platform business model)
- COGS: 25% (cloud infrastructure, payment processing, support)
- Basis: Enterprise gross margin is 78%; assumes SMB slightly lower
- Confidence: MODERATE (depends on support model; could be 70-80%)

SENSITIVITY:
Top 3 variables with most impact on profitability:
1. Customer acquisition cost (¬±$2K = ¬±$3M 3-year impact)
2. Market capture rate (¬±0.5% = ¬±$5M 3-year impact)
3. Gross margin (¬±5% = ¬±$2M 3-year impact)

If CAC is $7K instead of $5K: Payback extends to 24 months (less attractive)
If market capture is 1% instead of 2%: Revenue cut in half
If gross margin is 70% instead of 75%: Profitability delayed 6 months
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Assumptions for every line item
- ‚ùå Perfect validation
- ‚ùå Exhaustive sensitivity analysis
- ‚ùå Academic-level rigor

---

### 3. Calculations Are Correct & Transparent ‚úì

- [ ] **Model calculations are correct**
  - Are formulas correct?
  - Are units consistent (dollars, customers, months)?
  - Do calculations flow logically?
  - Can someone trace a calculation from input to output?

- [ ] **Calculation methodology is documented**
  - How is revenue calculated?
  - How are costs calculated?
  - How are key metrics derived?
  - Would someone understand the logic?

- [ ] **Model has been validated**
  - Have calculations been spot-checked?
  - Have formulas been reviewed?
  - Are outputs reasonable?
  - Would finance team review this?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
REVENUE CALCULATION:
Year 1 Revenue = New Customers in Year 1 √ó Avg Annual Price + Renewal Revenue
New Customers Year 1 = 50 customers (ramp from 0 to 50 over year)
Avg Annual Price = $20K
Year 1 Revenue = (50 √ó $20K) + $0 (no renewals yet) = $1M

GROSS MARGIN CALCULATION:
Year 1 Gross Profit = Revenue - COGS
Year 1 COGS = Revenue √ó 25% (cloud, payment processing, support)
Year 1 COGS = $1M √ó 25% = $250K
Year 1 Gross Profit = $1M - $250K = $750K
Year 1 Gross Margin = $750K / $1M = 75%

OPERATING EXPENSE CALCULATION:
Year 1 OpEx = Team costs + Marketing + Sales + G&A
Team costs: 5 people √ó $150K = $750K
Marketing: $250K (customer acquisition campaigns)
Sales (covered in team): Included above
G&A: $100K (shared services)
Total Year 1 OpEx = $750K + $250K + $100K = $1.1M

EBITDA CALCULATION:
Year 1 EBITDA = Gross Profit - OpEx = $750K - $1.1M = -$350K (loss in Year 1)

CAC PAYBACK CALCULATION:
CAC = Total Sales & Marketing / New Customers
CAC = $400K / 50 customers = $8K per customer (closer to $8K than $5K assumed)
LTV = Gross Margin per Customer √ó Customer Lifetime
LTV = ($20K √ó 75%) √ó 3 years = $45K
CAC Payback = CAC / (Monthly Gross Profit per Customer)
CAC Payback = $8K / ($1,250/mo) = 6.4 months (good payback)

VALIDATION CHECKS:
‚úì Units are consistent (dollars, customers, years)
‚úì Formulas calculate correctly
‚úì Revenue logic makes sense (customer count √ó price)
‚úì Cost logic makes sense (team + marketing + overhead)
‚úì CAC payback is reasonable for SaaS
‚úì Profitability trajectory is realistic (loss Year 1, breakeven Year 2, profit Year 3)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Excel-level model sophistication
- ‚ùå Perfect formula documentation
- ‚ùå Complete input/output tables
- ‚ùå Audited accuracy

---

### 4. Scenarios Are Modeled (Base, Upside, Downside) ‚úì

- [ ] **Base case reflects most likely outcome**
  - What's most likely to happen?
  - Assumptions are realistic?
  - Financial results credible?
  - Would finance team agree this is most likely?

- [ ] **Upside scenario is optimistic but possible**
  - What if things go better than expected?
  - What variables are more optimistic?
  - Upside is achievable (not fantasy)?
  - How different from base case?

- [ ] **Downside scenario is conservative but realistic**
  - What if things go worse than expected?
  - What variables are more conservative?
  - Downside still viable (not catastrophic)?
  - How different from base case?

- [ ] **Scenarios help decision-making**
  - Do scenarios show range of outcomes?
  - Do they inform risk assessment?
  - Do they help with contingency planning?
  - Would they change recommendation?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
BASE CASE (Most Likely - 60% probability):
Year 1: 50 customers, $1M revenue, -$350K EBITDA
Year 2: 150 customers, $3M revenue, +$200K EBITDA, breakeven reached
Year 3: 250 customers, $5M revenue, +$900K EBITDA, profitable
3-Year Total: $9M revenue, $1.75M gross profit, $750K net EBITDA

Key assumptions: CAC $8K, LTV $45K, 75% margin, 6.4 month payback
Confidence: MODERATE (customer acquisition is key variable)

UPSIDE CASE (Optimistic - 20% probability):
Assumption changes: Better unit economics (CAC $5K, LTV $60K)
Year 1: 75 customers, $1.5M revenue, -$150K EBITDA
Year 2: 225 customers, $4.5M revenue, +$500K EBITDA, breakeven earlier
Year 3: 350 customers, $7M revenue, +$1.5M EBITDA, strong profitability
3-Year Total: $13M revenue, $2.6M gross profit, $1.85M net EBITDA

Scenario: Strong SMB adoption, efficient sales, higher retention
Impact: Revenue 44% higher; profitability achieved faster
Decision impact: Makes SMB investment even more attractive

DOWNSIDE CASE (Conservative - 20% probability):
Assumption changes: Tougher economics (CAC $10K, LTV $40K)
Year 1: 25 customers, $500K revenue, -$550K EBITDA
Year 2: 75 customers, $1.5M revenue, -$100K EBITDA, still losing
Year 3: 150 customers, $3M revenue, +$200K EBITDA, breakeven delayed
3-Year Total: $5M revenue, $1.25M gross profit, -$450K net EBITDA

Scenario: Slower adoption, higher customer acquisition cost
Impact: Revenue 45% lower; profitability delayed to Year 3
Decision impact: Still reaches breakeven by Year 3; acceptable risk

SCENARIO SUMMARY:
                  Base Case    Upside       Downside
Year 1 Revenue    $1.0M        $1.5M        $0.5M
Year 2 Revenue    $3.0M        $4.5M        $1.5M
Year 3 Revenue    $5.0M        $7.0M        $3.0M
Year 3 EBITDA     +$900K       +$1.5M       +$200K
Payback          18 months    12 months    24 months
Probability       60%          20%          20%
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Many scenarios (3 is standard)
- ‚ùå Perfect probability assignment
- ‚ùå Exhaustive scenario variations
- ‚ùå Monte Carlo simulation

---

### 5. Financial Viability is Demonstrated ‚úì

- [ ] **Model shows path to profitability**
  - Does model reach profitability?
  - Timeline is reasonable?
  - Path is credible?
  - Would finance team fund this?

- [ ] **Key metrics are healthy**
  - CAC payback period is acceptable?
  - LTV:CAC ratio is healthy (>3:1 typical)?
  - Gross margin is sustainable?
  - Burn rate is manageable?

- [ ] **Financial impact is clear**
  - Investment required for initiative is quantified
  - Expected return is articulated
  - Timeline to breakeven/profitability is clear
  - Risk/reward balance is visible

**What This Looks Like:**
```
VIABILITY ASSESSMENT:

PROFITABILITY TRAJECTORY:
Year 1: -$350K loss (investment phase)
Year 2: +$200K EBITDA (breakeven reached)
Year 3: +$900K EBITDA (scaled profitable)
Verdict: VIABLE - reaches profitability within 3 years

KEY METRICS (Base Case):
CAC: $8K / LTV: $45K ‚Üí LTV:CAC ratio = 5.6:1 ‚úì (Healthy, >3:1)
Gross Margin: 75% ‚úì (Healthy for SaaS)
Annual Burn Rate Year 1: $350K ‚úì (Manageable; can fund from enterprise cash)
Customer Payback: 6.4 months ‚úì (Acceptable; drives fast scaling)

FINANCIAL IMPACT:
- Total investment: $1.1M in Year 1 + $0.6M in Year 2 = $1.7M
- Expected return by Year 3: $5M annual revenue run-rate
- 3-year cumulative EBITDA: $750K
- Simple payback on investment: 2.3 years
- ROI: 44% annually (good for strategic initiative)
- Verdict: ATTRACTIVE - solid returns justify investment

FINANCIAL RISK:
- If CAC is $10K (vs. $8K assumed): Payback 2.7 years (still acceptable)
- If LTV is $40K (vs. $45K assumed): Payback 2.5 years (still acceptable)
- If adoption slower: Still profitable by Year 3
- Verdict: ACCEPTABLE RISK - even in downside, returns viable
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect financial returns
- ‚ùå Immediate profitability
- ‚ùå Zero-risk scenarios
- ‚ùå Complete financial analysis

---

### 6. Supporting Materials Are Clear ‚úì

- [ ] **Model outputs are visualized**
  - Are key financial projections shown clearly?
  - Charts or tables for revenue, margin, profitability?
  - Easy to see trajectory over time?
  - Can someone understand financials at a glance?

- [ ] **Assumptions are easy to find**
  - Are key assumptions documented?
  - Can someone see what's driving outcomes?
  - Easy to modify assumptions and see impact?
  - Clear how to stress-test model?

- [ ] **Documentation is complete**
  - Is model structure explained?
  - Are calculations transparent?
  - Could someone use model or understand it?
  - Is there sufficient context?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
PRESENTATION:

CHART 1: Revenue Projection (3 scenarios)
- Line chart showing Base/Upside/Downside over 3 years
- Easy to see revenue trajectory
- Can visually compare scenarios

CHART 2: Path to Profitability
- Waterfall showing revenue ‚Üí margin ‚Üí OpEx ‚Üí EBITDA
- Shows which factors drive profitability
- Easy to see where value is created

TABLE 1: Key Assumptions
- Lists all critical assumptions
- Shows base/upside/downside values
- Notes rationale and confidence level
- Easy to identify most sensitive variables

TABLE 2: Financial Summary
- 3-year revenue, margin, EBITDA by scenario
- Key metrics (CAC, LTV, payback)
- Comparison of scenarios
- Easy to see financial viability

DOCUMENTATION:
- Model scope (what's included)
- Calculation methodology (how numbers derived)
- Assumption rationale (why we believe each)
- Sensitivity analysis (impact of key variables)
- Data sources (where assumptions come from)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Beautiful charting
- ‚ùå Multiple visualizations
- ‚ùå Polished presentation design
- ‚ùå Interactive tools

---

## Enhancing Criteria (Improving Quality)

These items strengthen the model but aren't strictly blocking:

- [ ] **Unit economics are detailed**
  - Revenue per customer documented
  - Cost per customer documented
  - Margin per customer clear
  - Scaling economics visible

- [ ] **Cohort analysis included**
  - New vs. renewal customers tracked
  - Retention dynamics modeled
  - Cohort profitability clear
  - Helps understand sustainable unit economics

- [ ] **Cash flow is modeled**
  - Cash position projected
  - Working capital considered
  - Timing of cash needs clear
  - Runway/funding requirements identified

- [ ] **Sensitivity to key risks**
  - What if customer acquisition is slower?
  - What if retention is lower?
  - What if pricing pressure?
  - What if competitive response?

- [ ] **Comparison to benchmarks**
  - How do metrics compare to industry?
  - How do metrics compare to competitors?
  - Are we optimistic/pessimistic?
  - Do benchmarks validate assumptions?

---

## Quality Checks (Before Approving)

Before confirming model is complete, ask yourself:

1. **Would finance team trust this model?**
   - Are assumptions credible?
   - Are calculations correct?
   - Is profitability realistic?
   - Would they fund this?

2. **Does model support decision-making?**
   - Is financial viability clear?
   - Is investment requirement clear?
   - Is expected return clear?
   - Would this change a decision?

3. **Are key risks captured?**
   - What would break this model?
   - Are downside scenarios realistic?
   - Are mitigations possible?
   - Is risk/reward acceptable?

4. **Could someone modify assumptions?**
   - Is model structure clear?
   - Can scenarios be adjusted?
   - Would changes cascade correctly?
   - Is model flexible enough?

---

## Readiness Assessment

### ‚úÖ Model is Ready When

All blocking criteria are met:
- Model scope and structure are clear
- Key assumptions are documented and realistic
- Calculations are correct and transparent
- Scenarios (base, upside, downside) are modeled
- Financial viability is demonstrated
- Supporting materials are clear
- Documentation is complete

**Model can support strategic financial decisions.**

---

### üîÑ Model Needs More Work When

- **Assumptions unclear?** ‚Üí Document all key assumptions
- **Calculations wrong?** ‚Üí Fix formulas and recalculate
- **No scenarios?** ‚Üí Build base/upside/downside cases
- **Viability questionable?** ‚Üí Adjust assumptions or revisit strategy
- **Hard to understand?** ‚Üí Improve documentation and visualization
- **Data incomplete?** ‚Üí Gather missing information or use estimates

---

## Common Issues & Resolution

| Issue | Signal | Resolution |
|-------|--------|-----------|
| **Too optimistic** | "This seems unrealistic" | Validate assumptions; compare to benchmarks |
| **Missing key cost** | "COGS seems too low" | Identify all costs; validate with ops |
| **Calculations inconsistent** | "Numbers don't match" | Check formulas; ensure consistency |
| **No downside scenario** | "What if it fails?" | Build conservative scenario |
| **Assumptions vague** | "Why is CAC $5K?" | Document rationale and confidence |
| **Too complex** | "Can't follow logic" | Simplify; focus on key drivers |

---

## Post-Validation Actions

Once this checklist passes:

1. **Review with Finance**
   - Finance team validates model
   - Addresses any concerns
   - Gets buy-in on assumptions
   - Confirms financial viability

2. **Use for Decision-Making**
   - Present financials to executives
   - Address financial questions
   - Use to support/challenge strategy
   - Incorporate into decision framework

3. **Establish Monitoring**
   - Set up tracking of actual vs. forecast
   - Plan monthly/quarterly reviews
   - Identify early warning signals
   - Plan course corrections

4. **Archive for Reference**
   - Save model and documentation
   - Reference for future decisions
   - Use for learning (actual vs. forecast)
   - Build financial forecasting capability

---

==================== START: financial-modeling-quality-checklist ====================
# Financial Modeling Quality Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that financial models have transparent assumptions, sound methodology, properly calculated projections, and sensitivity analysis sufficient to support investment and strategic decisions.

## What Gets Validated

**Task Reference:** `tasks/financial-modeling.md`

**Used In:** ANALYSE and DECIDE phases for financial projections and business case validation

**Audience:** CFO, finance team, investment decision-makers

---

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. Model Assumptions Are Transparent & Justified ‚úì

- [ ] **Key assumptions are listed and stated clearly**
  - Revenue assumptions (growth rate, ACV, churn)
  - Cost assumptions (COGS, OpEx, headcount, etc.)
  - Capital assumptions (funding needed, timing)
  - Timeline/macroeconomic assumptions
  - All major assumptions documented

- [ ] **Each assumption is justified**
  - Why this revenue growth rate?
  - Why this cost structure?
  - What data supports assumption?
  - How was assumption derived?
  - Alternative assumption ranges provided?

- [ ] **Assumption changes are tracked**
  - What assumptions changed from previous model?
  - Why were assumptions updated?
  - What's the impact of changes?
  - Is change log maintained?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
FINANCIAL MODEL ASSUMPTIONS:

REVENUE ASSUMPTIONS:

Assumption: Year 1 ACV = $50K; grows 5% annually
Justification:
- Competitive pricing analysis shows $40-70K typical ACV
- Our positioning is mid-premium; $50K is justified
- Growth due to: longer implementation = higher ACV; land and expand
Data source: 5 comparable companies; our market research
Confidence: MEDIUM-HIGH

Alternative ranges tested:
- Conservative: $40K ACV (5% growth)
- Base case: $50K ACV (5% growth)
- Optimistic: $60K ACV (8% growth)
See sensitivity section for impact

Assumption: Year 1 customer acquisition = 3 customers
Justification:
- Conservative entry (market validation phase)
- Sales team building (not yet at full capacity)
- Implementation capacity constraint (3-6 month cycles)
- Ramps to 15 customers by Year 3; 40+ by Year 5
Data source: Comparable company growth curves; our sales timeline
Confidence: MEDIUM (depends on market acceptance and sales execution)

Alternative ranges:
- Conservative: 2 customers Year 1 (slower ramp)
- Base case: 3 customers Year 1
- Optimistic: 5 customers Year 1 (faster adoption)

Assumption: Year 1 churn = 0%; stabilizes at 5% annual by Year 3
Justification:
- Early customers: unlikely to churn (hand-held, engaged)
- By Year 3: stabilize at industry average (5-8%)
- Steady-state churn: 5% annual
Data source: Industry benchmarks; SaaS retention curves
Confidence: MEDIUM (churn unknown until we have customers)

---

COST ASSUMPTIONS:

Assumption: COGS = 20% of revenue (support and hosting costs)
Justification:
- Support: 1 FTE supports 10-15 customers at $50K ACV
- Hosting/infrastructure: $5K/month + variable
- Maintenance/updates: 10% of revenue
Data source: Industry benchmarks; comparable companies
Confidence: MEDIUM-HIGH (depends on support model and scale)

Assumption: Sales + Marketing = $2.5M Year 1; 40% of revenue Year 2-3
Justification:
- Year 1: Building sales team; heavy marketing investment (no revenue yet)
- Year 2-3: Mature ratio is 40% of revenue (SaaS benchmark)
- Includes: 3 sales reps (Year 1); ramping to 8 by Year 5
Data source: SaaS benchmarks; our headcount plan
Confidence: MEDIUM (assumes sales execution; variable costs could be higher)

Assumption: Product development = 35% of revenue ongoing
Justification:
- Ongoing feature development; bug fixes; tech debt
- Industry standard for product companies
- Includes: VP Product + 5-7 engineers
Data source: SaaS benchmarks; our org plan
Confidence: MEDIUM-HIGH

---

CAPITAL ASSUMPTIONS:

Assumption: Initial capital needed = $3M for first 18 months
Justification:
- Covers: Product development ($1.2M); Sales/Marketing ($1.0M); G&A ($0.8M)
- Runway: 18 months to reach inflection (profitability path clear)
- Timing: $2M upfront; $1M in Month 12 (contingency)
Data source: Detailed headcount plan; spending forecast
Confidence: MEDIUM-HIGH (detailed budget; some contingency)

---

MACRO ASSUMPTIONS:

Assumption: Market grows 12% annually (supply chain optimization)
Justification:
- Digital transformation drives adoption
- Post-COVID supply chain investment continues
- Industry analyst forecasts 10-15% growth
Data source: Gartner; IDC; industry reports
Confidence: MEDIUM (macro trends could change)

Assumption: No major economic recession during 5-year period
Justification:
- Base case assumes normal economic cycle
- Sensitivity tested for recession scenario
- SMB customer base somewhat recession-resistant (essentials)
Data source: Economic forecasts; sensitivity analysis
Confidence: LOW (economy is unpredictable)

---

ASSUMPTION CHANGE LOG:

Version 1.0 (6 months ago):
- Year 1 ACV: $40K (now $50K due to competitive positioning)
- Year 1 customer acquisition: 5 (now 3 due to implementation constraints)
- COGS: 25% (now 20% due to ops efficiency improvements)
- Impact: Year 3 profitability pushed out 6 months

Version 2.0 (3 months ago):
- Sales & Marketing: 45% of revenue (now 40% due to more efficient GTM)
- Churn assumption: 8% stable (now 5% due to better product/support)
- Impact: Year 4 profitability improved significantly
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Assumption change for every version
- ‚ùå Formal approval for every assumption
- ‚ùå Unanimous agreement on assumptions
- ‚ùå Perfect data backing every assumption

### 2. Model Methodology Is Sound ‚úì

- [ ] **Model structure is logical**
  - Revenue section clearly defined
  - Cost section clearly defined
  - Profitability/cash flow clearly calculated
  - Easy to follow logic flow
  - Could be verified by someone else

- [ ] **Calculations are accurate**
  - Are spreadsheet formulas correct?
  - Are calculations tested (spot-check)?
  - Are circular references avoided?
  - Are sources/targets clear?

- [ ] **Sensitivity is built in**
  - Can assumptions be easily changed?
  - Are scenarios modeled (best/base/worst)?
  - Impact of key assumption changes shown?
  - Is sensitivity range realistic?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
FINANCIAL MODEL STRUCTURE:

SECTION 1: REVENUE PROJECTION (5-year)
Inputs (assumptions):
- Starting ACV: $50K
- Annual customer acquisition: Year 1=3; Year 2=8; Year 3=15; etc.
- Annual churn rate: 0% Years 1-2; 5% Years 3-5
- ACV growth: 5% annually (land and expand)

Calculations:
Year 1:
- New customers: 3
- Starting customers: 0
- Churned customers: 0
- Ending customers: 3
- Average ACV (conservative): $45K (weighted by acquisition timing)
- Annual recurring revenue: 3 √ó $45K = $135K

Year 2:
- Starting customers: 3
- New customers: 8
- Churned customers: 0.15 (5% √ó 3, assume mid-year)
- Ending customers: 10.85 ‚âà 11
- Average ACV: $47K (2-year average; growth on new + existing)
- ARR: 11 √ó $47K = $517K

Year 3:
- Starting customers: 11
- New customers: 15
- Churned customers: 0.55 (5% √ó 11)
- Ending customers: 25.45 ‚âà 25
- Average ACV: $49K
- ARR: 25 √ó $49K = $1.225M

Year 4-5: Similar logic

OUTPUT: 5-year revenue projection ($135K ‚Üí $5.2M)

SECTION 2: COST PROJECTION (5-year)
Inputs (assumptions):
- COGS: 20% of revenue (support, hosting)
- Sales & Marketing: $2.5M Year 1; 40% of revenue Year 2+
- Product dev: 35% of revenue
- G&A: $500K Year 1; 12% of revenue Year 2+
- Headcount: Starting 8 (including founders); growing to 45 by Year 5

Calculations:
Year 1:
- Gross profit: $135K revenue - 20% COGS ($27K) = $108K
- Gross margin: 80%
- OpEx: Sales/Mkt ($2.5M) + Product ($47K) + G&A ($500K) = $3.047M
- EBITDA: $108K - $3.047M = -$2.939M
- Headcount: 8

Year 2:
- Gross profit: $517K - 20% ($103K) = $414K
- Gross margin: 80%
- OpEx: 40% sales/mkt ($207K) + 35% product ($181K) + 12% G&A ($62K) = $450K
- EBITDA: $414K - $450K = -$36K (near breakeven)
- Headcount: 12

Year 3:
- Gross profit: $1.225M - 20% ($245K) = $980K
- Gross margin: 80%
- OpEx: 40% sales/mkt ($490K) + 35% product ($429K) + 12% G&A ($147K) = $1.066M
- EBITDA: $980K - $1.066M = -$86K (near breakeven)
- Headcount: 18

Year 4:
- Revenue: $3.1M
- EBITDA: $300K (profitable!)

Year 5:
- Revenue: $5.2M
- EBITDA: $900K

OUTPUT: 5-year cost structure and profitability path

SECTION 3: CASH FLOW PROJECTION
Inputs (assumptions):
- Upfront capital: $3M
- Customer collection: Net 30 (assume monthly)
- Capital expenditure: Minimal (SaaS model)
- Payroll timing: Monthly, consistent
- Quarterly board/investor payouts: None until profitable

Calculations:
Year 1:
- Beginning cash: $3M
- Operating cash flow: -$2.939M (EBITDA from above)
- CapEx: $0 (minimal for SaaS)
- Financing: $0 (no additional raise assumed in base case)
- Ending cash: $3M - $2.939M = $61K
- Cash runway: Tight (need contingency capital)

Year 2:
- Beginning cash: $61K
- Operating cash flow: -$36K (near breakeven helps)
- Ending cash: $25K
- Cash runway: Very tight (contingency needed)

Year 3:
- Beginning cash: $25K
- Operating cash flow: -$86K (not yet profitable)
- Issues: Negative cash flow continues; will need additional capital or faster ramp

RECOMMENDATION: Model shows need for $3.5M capital (not just $3M) for 18-month runway to profitable growth.

MODEL VERIFICATION:
Spot checks:
‚úì Year 1 revenue: 3 customers √ó $50K = $150K (within 10% of modeled $135K; difference is timing)
‚úì Year 2 COGS: $517K √ó 20% = $103K ‚úì
‚úì Year 2 OpEx: Correctly calculated
‚úì Cash flow: Consistent with EBITDA

Testing:
‚úì Circular references: None identified
‚úì Formulas: Spot-checked 5+ cells; all correct
‚úì Sources: Assumptions clearly linked to revenue/cost tabs
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect spreadsheet polish
- ‚ùå Peer review (though valuable)
- ‚ùå Formal audit
- ‚ùå Multi-page documentation

### 3. Key Financial Metrics Are Calculated ‚úì

- [ ] **Profitability metrics are clear**
  - When does business become profitable?
  - What's the path to profitability?
  - What's the margin structure?
  - How does profitability compare to benchmarks?

- [ ] **Cash flow metrics are calculated**
  - When do we run out of cash?
  - What's the cash burn rate?
  - When is payback period?
  - How much capital is needed?

- [ ] **Unit economics are modeled**
  - Customer acquisition cost (CAC)?
  - Customer lifetime value (LTV)?
  - LTV:CAC ratio (rule of thumb: >3:1)?
  - Payback period (rule of thumb: <12 months)?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
KEY FINANCIAL METRICS:

PROFITABILITY:

Gross Margin: 80% (consistent Years 1-5)
- Industry benchmark: 75-85% for SaaS
- Our model: On target

Operating Margin by Year:
- Year 1: -2900% (heavy investment phase)
- Year 2: -7% (near breakeven)
- Year 3: -7% (still investing)
- Year 4: 10% (profitable!)
- Year 5: 17% (maturing)
- Trajectory: Reasonable for SaaS company

Payback Period: ~36 months (3 years)
- Year 1-2: Building product and sales
- Year 3: Near breakeven
- Year 4: Profitable; recovering initial investment
- Benchmark: SaaS payback often 2-4 years
- Assessment: Reasonable; slightly long but acceptable given market entry risk

---

CASH FLOW:

Monthly Burn Rate (Year 1):
- Total spending: $3.047M √∑ 12 = $254K/month
- Revenue: Minimal initially
- Net burn: ~$250K/month
- Runway with $3M: 12 months (need extend to 18)

Cash Runway:
- Starting capital: $3M
- Monthly burn: $250K (declining over year)
- Additional capital needed: $500K - $1M for contingency
- Recommendation: Raise $3.5M (not just $3M)

Payback of Initial Investment:
- Initial investment: $3M
- Cumulative EBITDA recovery:
  Year 1: -$2.9M (behind by $2.9M)
  Year 2: -$2.9M - $36K = -$2.936M (still underwater)
  Year 3: -$2.936M - $86K = -$3.022M (worse!)
  Year 4: -$3.022M + $300K = -$2.722M (recovering)
  Year 5: -$2.722M + $900K = -$1.822M

Payback analysis: Not achieved by Year 5 in base case
Issues: Model shows investment not fully recovered by Year 5
This suggests either:
1. Model is too conservative (likely)
2. Growth needs to accelerate
3. Additional capital beyond $3M will be needed
4. Exit strategy (acquisition) needed for returns

---

UNIT ECONOMICS:

Customer Acquisition Cost (CAC):
Year 1:
- Sales & Marketing spend: $2.5M
- Customers acquired: 3
- CAC: $2.5M √∑ 3 = $833K per customer
- This is HIGH (bloated by fixed costs; Year 1 is inefficient)

Year 2:
- Sales & Marketing spend: $207K
- Customers acquired: 8
- CAC: $207K √∑ 8 = $26K per customer
- More realistic (sales team now productive)

Year 3-5:
- CAC stabilizes around $20-30K per customer
- Benchmark: For $50K ACV, CAC of $20-30K is reasonable (LTV:CAC ‚âà 3:1)

Customer Lifetime Value (LTV):
Assumptions:
- Average customer lifetime: 7 years (1 √∑ 5% churn)
- Annual ACV: Grows 5% per year over lifetime
- Year 1 customer: $50K
- Year 2 customer: $52.5K average over lifetime
- Gross margin: 80% (what we keep)

Calculation:
Year 1 customer LTV:
- Year 1: $50K √ó 80% = $40K
- Year 2: $50K √ó 1.05 √ó 80% = $42K
- Year 3-7: Similar growth
- Total LTV: ~$330K (rough estimate)

LTV:CAC Ratio (Year 2 forward):
- LTV: $330K
- CAC: $25K (average)
- Ratio: 330 √∑ 25 = 13:1
- Benchmark: >3:1 is healthy; we're at 13:1 (excellent)
- Implication: Strong unit economics; customers are very profitable

CAC Payback Period:
- Annual ACV: $50K (Year 1 customer)
- Annual gross profit: $50K √ó 80% = $40K
- CAC: $25K (amortized Year 2+)
- Payback: $25K √∑ $40K = 0.625 years ‚âà 7.5 months
- Benchmark: <12 months is good; we're at 7.5 months (excellent)
- Implication: Fast payback; capital efficient

---

METRICS SUMMARY:

Profitability Path: Good (reaches profitability Year 4)
Unit Economics: Excellent (13:1 LTV:CAC; 7.5 month payback)
Cash Runway: Tight (need more capital; recommend $3.5M)
Overall Assessment: Strong business fundamentals; capital dependent
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Every possible metric
- ‚ùå Perfect calculation accuracy
- ‚ùå Formal financial analysis
- ‚ùå Comparison to all benchmarks
