==================== START: solution-design-quality-checklist ====================
# Solution Design Quality Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that proposed solutions address root causes, are technically feasible, have acceptable trade-offs, and can realistically be executed within constraints.

## What Gets Validated

**Task Reference:** `tasks/solution-design.md`

**Used In:** ACT phase for solution validation before execution planning

**Audience:** Solution architects, implementation leaders, executives

---

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. Solution Directly Addresses Root Causes ‚úì

- [ ] **Solution targets identified root causes**
  - Does solution address the core problem (not symptom)?
  - Would fixing solution actually solve problem?
  - Are root causes directly addressed?
  - Would skeptic accept solution logic?

- [ ] **Solution logic is clear**
  - How does solution fix root cause?
  - What's the mechanism of change?
  - Why would this work?
  - Could be explained simply?

- [ ] **Alternative solutions were considered**
  - Were other approaches explored?
  - Why was this solution chosen?
  - What trade-offs were made?
  - Are alternatives documented?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
ROOT CAUSE vs. SOLUTION:

Root Cause Identified: "SMB market gap exists; competitors filling it"
  (Not: "Customers are churning")
  (Not: "We're not competitive")

Solution 1: Build separate SMB product
- Logic: Address market gap by building product for SMB
- Why it works: Competes directly in gap competitors filled
- Trade-off: Resource split; complexity; longer development
- Assessment: Directly addresses root cause ‚úì

Solution 2: Lower pricing on existing product
- Logic: Make existing product affordable for SMB
- Why it works: Removes price barrier; competes on value
- Trade-off: Margin compression; possible brand damage
- Assessment: Partially addresses (removes price barrier; not full gap)

Solution 3: Partner with implementer for SMB
- Logic: Partner delivers simplified implementation
- Why it works: Addresses complexity; provides SMB solution
- Trade-off: Revenue sharing; less direct control
- Assessment: Partially addresses (removes complexity; not full gap)

Recommended: Solution 1 (most directly addresses root cause)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect logic proof
- ‚ùå Exhaustive alternatives analysis
- ‚ùå Unanimous stakeholder agreement
- ‚ùå Guaranteed success

---

### 2. Solution Feasibility Is Assessed ‚úì

- [ ] **Technical feasibility is clear**
  - Can we build/deliver this?
  - What's the technical challenge?
  - Do we have capability or need to develop?
  - What's realistic timeline?

- [ ] **Resource feasibility is clear**
  - What resources are required?
  - Do we have them or need to acquire?
  - What's the cost?
  - Are resources available?

- [ ] **Execution feasibility is clear**
  - Can we realistically execute this?
  - What's the biggest execution risk?
  - What operational changes needed?
  - Is execution realistic?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
FEASIBILITY ASSESSMENT:

Solution: Build separate SMB product

Technical Feasibility:
- Challenge: Build simplified product (vs. enterprise complexity)
- Capability: We have core technology; need simplification
- Timeline: 6 months to MVP (realistic for scope)
- Risk: MEDIUM (doable; requires focus)

Resource Feasibility:
- Team needed: 1 PM + 3-4 engineers + 1 QA
- Cost: $400-500K for 6 months
- Availability: Can reallocate from enterprise product
- Risk: MEDIUM (requires reallocation; opportunity cost)

Execution Feasibility:
- Key risk: Maintaining enterprise product while building SMB
- Mitigation: Dedicate team; separate execution tracks
- Operational changes: Separate product roadmap; GTM; support
- Risk: MEDIUM (dual-track execution is complex)

Overall Feasibility: MEDIUM (doable; requires careful execution)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Detailed project plans
- ‚ùå Perfect resource estimates
- ‚ùå Zero execution risk
- ‚ùå Low-risk solutions only

---

### 3. Solution Trade-Offs Are Explicit ‚úì

- [ ] **What we gain is clear**
  - What benefits does solution provide?
  - How does it improve situation?
  - What value is created?
  - Is gain significant?

- [ ] **What we give up is clear**
  - What costs are incurred?
  - What opportunities are foregone?
  - What risks are accepted?
  - Are costs acceptable?

- [ ] **Trade-off analysis is documented**
  - Benefits vs. costs clearly compared
  - Is trade-off worthwhile?
  - Would stakeholder agree?
  - Is choice defensible?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
TRADE-OFF ANALYSIS:

Solution: Build separate SMB product

What We Gain:
+ Address SMB market gap (large addressable market)
+ Capture churned SMB customers (recover revenue)
+ Establish SMB market leadership (competitive advantage)
+ Premium positioning for enterprise (focus on strength)
+ Potential for higher total revenue ($5M+ SMB opportunity)

What We Give Up:
- Engineering resources split (slows enterprise product)
- Marketing/sales resources split (divided focus)
- Support resources split (need dual support model)
- Profitability delayed (investment in SMB)
- Organizational complexity (dual product management)
- Brand confusion (enterprise vs. SMB positioning)

Quantified Trade-Off:
- Investment: $500K + $1M/year GTM + support
- Expected return: $3-5M additional revenue by Year 3
- ROI: 2-5x on investment; timeline 3+ years
- Risk: Execution complexity; market adoption uncertainty

Assessment:
Benefits >> Costs (worthwhile trade-off)
But requires:
- Clear execution plan
- Sufficient capital
- Organizational commitment
- Risk tolerance for parallel execution
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect quantification of trade-offs
- ‚ùå Unanimous agreement
- ‚ùå Risk-free choice
- ‚ùå Clear winner in all dimensions

---

### 4. Solution Has Realistic Constraints ‚úì

- [ ] **Financial constraints are acknowledged**
  - How much capital is available?
  - Is solution within budget?
  - What's the payback period?
  - Are constraints realistic?

- [ ] **Timeline constraints are acknowledged**
  - What's the required timeline?
  - Can solution be delivered in timeline?
  - What are the critical path items?
  - Are constraints realistic?

- [ ] **Risk constraints are acknowledged**
  - What level of risk is acceptable?
  - Does solution fit risk profile?
  - Are risks manageable?
  - Are constraints realistic?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
CONSTRAINTS:

Financial Constraint:
- Available capital: $3.5M for next 18 months
- SMB product investment: $500K upfront + $1M/year = $1.5M
- Remaining budget: $2M for other needs
- Assessment: Solution fits within financial constraint ‚úì

Timeline Constraint:
- Need SMB product by: Month 12 (18 months to profitability)
- Development timeline: 6 months (realistic)
- Market launch: Month 6
- Assessment: Solution fits within timeline constraint ‚úì

Risk Constraint:
- Risk tolerance: MEDIUM (can accept execution risk; not existential)
- Solution risk: MEDIUM (dual-track execution; market adoption)
- Assessment: Solution fits within risk constraint ‚úì

Overall: Solution is feasible within all constraints
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Exact constraint quantification
- ‚ùå Zero constraint violations
- ‚ùå Conservative timeline/budget
- ‚ùå Unanimous constraint agreement

---

### 5. Solution Has Success Criteria ‚úì

- [ ] **Criteria for "solution working" defined**
  - How do we measure success?
  - What metrics matter?
  - What's acceptable vs. unacceptable?
  - How will we know if working?

- [ ] **Interim milestones defined**
  - What are key checkpoints?
  - What's the measurement approach?
  - When do we assess?
  - What's acceptable at each stage?

- [ ] **Go/No-Go Decision Points Defined**
  - When do we decide if solution working?
  - What would cause pivot/termination?
  - Who decides?
  - What's the contingency?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
SUCCESS CRITERIA:

Ultimate Success (Year 3):
- SMB product is profitable (EBITDA positive)
- SMB revenue is $3M+ annually
- SMB customer NPS is 60+ (satisfied)
- SMB churn is <8% (retention strong)
- Enterprise product unharmed (churn remains <5%)

Interim Milestones:

Month 6 (Product Launch):
- MVP product ready for beta
- 3-5 pilot customers recruited
- Implementation process documented
- Support model ready
- GO/NO-GO: If <3 pilot customers or product not ready ‚Üí Extend timeline

Month 9 (Pilot Results):
- 3-5 customers go live
- Customer NPS >50 (positive feedback)
- Implementation takes <45 days (on track)
- GO/NO-GO: If NPS <40 or implementation >60 days ‚Üí Product refinement needed

Month 12 (Market Launch):
- 5-10 customers acquired
- $500K+ ARR (on track for plan)
- Sales process proven
- GO/NO-GO: If <5 customers or <$500K ARR ‚Üí Reconsider GTM approach

Month 18 (Scale Assessment):
- 20+ customers acquired
- $1.5M+ ARR (on track)
- Churn <8% (retention strong)
- GO/NO-GO: If <15 customers or >8% churn ‚Üí Assess market fit

Contingency Actions:
- If adoption slower: Extend timeline; reduce investment
- If churn higher: Improve product/support; adjust target market
- If enterprise affected: Reallocate resources; protect core business
- If market rejects: Pivot to adjacent vertical or business model
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect metrics
- ‚ùå All possible success criteria
- ‚ùå Quantified decision thresholds
- ‚ùå Unanimous agreement on criteria

---

### 6. Solution Is Communicated Clearly ‚úì

- [ ] **Solution description is clear**
  - Can someone understand solution from description?
  - Is it specific (not vague)?
  - Could be explained in 2 minutes?
  - Is logic easy to follow?

- [ ] **Solution documentation is complete**
  - Problem statement included?
  - Solution approach explained?
  - Trade-offs documented?
  - Feasibility assessment included?

- [ ] **Solution is ready for decision**
  - Is documentation executive-ready?
  - Would decision-maker approve?
  - Are key questions answered?
  - Is next action clear?

**What This Looks Like:**

```
SOLUTION DOCUMENTATION STRUCTURE:

1-Page Executive Summary:
- Problem: SMB market gap; competitors filling it; $5M churn
- Solution: Build separate SMB product offering
- Investment: $1.5M over 18 months
- Expected return: $3M+ SMB revenue by Year 3
- Timeline: MVP Month 6; Market launch Month 12
- Recommendation: Approve; proceed with detailed planning

Supporting Documentation (5-10 pages):
1. Problem Analysis
   - Root causes identified
   - Market opportunity validated
   - Competitive threat quantified

2. Solution Approach
   - Product strategy (separate SMB product)
   - Go-to-market approach
   - Resource plan
   - Timeline

3. Feasibility Assessment
   - Technical feasibility (MEDIUM; 6-month timeline)
   - Resource feasibility (MEDIUM; reallocation needed)
   - Financial feasibility (MEDIUM; $1.5M investment)

4. Trade-Off Analysis
   - Benefits: Market opportunity; revenue; competitive positioning
   - Costs: Resource split; organizational complexity
   - Overall: Benefits significantly outweigh costs

5. Risk Assessment
   - Key risks identified (dual-track execution; market adoption)
   - Mitigation approaches outlined
   - Contingency plans prepared

6. Success Criteria
   - Interim milestones defined (Month 6, 9, 12, 18)
   - Go/No-Go decision points established
   - Contingency actions identified

Clarity Check:
‚úì Can decision-maker understand solution? YES
‚úì Are key questions answered? YES
‚úì Is recommendation clear? YES
‚úì Is next step obvious? YES
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect documentation polish
- ‚ùå Multi-page detailed plans
- ‚ùå Formal presentations
- ‚ùå Academic rigor

---

## Enhancing Criteria (Improving Quality)

These items strengthen the solution but aren't strictly blocking:

- [ ] **Customer validation of solution**
  - Have customers indicated preference for this solution?
  - Would customers want this solution?
  - Customer willingness to adopt validation?

- [ ] **Competitive implications clear**
  - How does this solution affect competitive positioning?
  - Does competitor have similar approach?
  - Do we have advantage with this approach?

- [ ] **Organizational alignment assessed**
  - Does leadership agree this is right solution?
  - Are there alternative solutions preferred?
  - Can organization commit to this approach?

- [ ] **Phased implementation approach**
  - Could solution be phased (reduce risk)?
  - What would Phase 1 look like?
  - What's the graduation path?

---

## Quality Checks (Before Approving)

Before confirming solution is complete, ask yourself:

1. **Does solution actually fix the problem?**
   - Would solving this eliminate the root cause?
   - Or is this a band-aid?
   - Would skeptic accept the logic?

2. **Is solution realistic to execute?**
   - Can we actually do this?
   - Do we have the resources?
   - Is timeline credible?

3. **Are trade-offs worth it?**
   - Do benefits outweigh costs?
   - Are we giving up too much?
   - Would stakeholder agree?

4. **Could solution fail?**
   - What could go wrong?
   - What would cause us to pivot?
   - Do we have contingencies?

---

## Readiness Assessment

### ‚úÖ Solution Design is Ready When

All blocking criteria are met:
- Solution directly addresses root causes
- Solution feasibility is assessed
- Trade-offs are explicit
- Solution has realistic constraints
- Success criteria are defined
- Solution is communicated clearly

**Solution can be handed to execution team with confidence.**

---

### üîÑ Solution Needs More Work When

- **Doesn't address root cause?** ‚Üí Refocus on actual problem
- **Feasibility unclear?** ‚Üí Research capability; get expert input
- **Trade-offs hidden?** ‚Üí Make explicit; quantify
- **No success criteria?** ‚Üí Define how to measure
- **Communication weak?** ‚Üí Clarify explanation
- **Constraints violated?** ‚Üí Adjust solution or constraints

---

## Post-Validation Actions

Once this checklist passes:

1. **Get Executive Approval**
   - Present solution to decision-maker
   - Address questions/concerns
   - Gain buy-in on approach
   - Confirm resource commitment

2. **Prepare Execution Team**
   - Transition to execution planning
   - Detailed project plan developed
   - Team assignments finalized
   - Success criteria reviewed

3. **Communicate Solution**
   - Share with broader organization
   - Explain rationale; get buy-in
   - Address concerns; answer questions
   - Build organizational alignment

4. **Monitor & Adjust**
   - Track progress vs. plan
   - Assess interim milestones
   - Make go/no-go decisions
   - Adjust if needed

---

## Sign-Off

**Solution Designed By:** __________________ (Strategy/Design Lead)

**Solution Reviewed By:** __________________ (Executive Sponsor)

**Date Completed:** __________________

**Confirmed Ready for Use:** ‚òê Yes ‚òê No

**If No, specific issues:**

---

## Related Resources

- **Task:** `tasks/solution-design.md`
- **Phase:** ACT phase (solution definition before execution)
- **Follow-up:** Execution planning; implementation management

==================== END: solution-design-quality-checklist ====================

==================== START: split-phase-completion-checklist ====================
# SPLIT Phase Completion Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that the SPLIT phase (Strategic Specialist) has completed all essential work before transitioning to the ANALYSE phase. This checklist ensures the problem or opportunity has been decomposed into analyzable components with clear hypotheses and investigation priorities.

## What This Phase Accomplishes

The SPLIT phase takes a complex problem and breaks it into manageable pieces. The Strategic Specialist ensures:
- The problem is systematically decomposed
- Root causes are theorized (not yet proven)
- Hypotheses are testable
- Analysis questions are prioritized
- Investigation approach is structured

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. Problem Decomposition ‚úì

- [ ] **Problem broken into logical components**
  - Problem structure is MECE (Mutually Exclusive, Collectively Exhaustive)
  - All aspects of problem addressed in decomposition
  - Components are at analyzable level (not too broad, not too granular)
  - Relationships between components identified

- [ ] **Problem structure is documented**
  - Issue tree or problem tree created
  - Each level logically justified
  - Major branches labeled clearly
  - Sub-components explicit and testable

- [ ] **Problem boundaries are maintained**
  - Decomposition respects original scope
  - Doesn't introduce new out-of-scope areas
  - Stays focused on the core challenge
  - Cross-functional dependencies noted

**What This Looks Like:**
```
Core Problem: Customer churn 15% annually ($5M ARR)
‚îú‚îÄ Why are customers leaving? (Root causes)
‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ Product dissatisfaction
‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ Competitive pressure
‚îÇ  ‚îî‚îÄ Price sensitivity
‚îú‚îÄ Who is leaving? (Segmentation)
‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ SMB segment
‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ Enterprise segment
‚îÇ  ‚îî‚îÄ Geographic variance
‚îî‚îÄ When are they leaving? (Timeline)
   ‚îú‚îÄ Within first 6 months
   ‚îú‚îÄ Year 1-2
   ‚îî‚îÄ Year 3+
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Detailed analysis of each branch
- ‚ùå Definitive root cause identification
- ‚ùå Complete stakeholder input on structure
- ‚ùå Perfect decomposition (good enough is fine)

---

### 2. Hypothesis Formation ‚úì

- [ ] **Root cause hypotheses formulated**
  - For each major problem branch, hypothesis stated
  - Hypotheses are testable ("If/Then" format)
  - Hypotheses are grounded in initial evidence or logic
  - Alternative hypotheses considered and noted

- [ ] **Hypotheses are prioritized**
  - High-impact hypotheses identified (biggest business effect if true)
  - High-probability hypotheses identified (most likely to be true)
  - Priority ranking established for investigation
  - Quick-win hypotheses separated from deep-dive ones

- [ ] **Hypothesis testing approach outlined**
  - For each hypothesis, testing approach identified
  - Data/evidence needed specified
  - Validation criteria defined (what proves/disproves?)
  - Relative effort estimated for each test

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Hypothesis 1 (High Impact/Probability):** "Customers in SMB segment churn because competitors offer lower prices"
  - Test: Compare pricing vs. top 3 competitors; interview churned SMB customers
  - Validation: "Supported if 60%+ of SMB churn cite price; refuted if less than 20%"

- **Hypothesis 2 (High Impact/Lower Probability):** "Product gaps in mobile experience drive enterprise churn"
  - Test: Feature gap analysis; NPS analysis by customer type; interviews
  - Validation: "Supported if mobile is top 3 pain point for 40%+ enterprise customers"

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Definitive proof of hypotheses
- ‚ùå Complete testing methodology
- ‚ùå Quantified probability estimates
- ‚ùå Perfect hypothesis wording

---

### 3. Analysis Framework ‚úì

- [ ] **Analysis work plan created**
  - All analysis tasks identified (what analyses are needed?)
  - Sequencing established (what order makes sense?)
  - Dependencies noted (which analyses inform others?)
  - Resource requirements estimated

- [ ] **Key investigation questions defined**
  - For each problem component, key questions listed
  - Questions are specific and answerable
  - Questions connected to hypotheses
  - Answers will inform decisions

- [ ] **Data gaps and sources identified**
  - What data exists internally (available, accessible)
  - What external research is needed
  - What interviews/primary research required
  - Feasibility of gathering each type assessed

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Investigation Questions for Product Dissatisfaction:**
  - "What specific features are customers requesting most?"
  - "How does our feature set compare to competitors?"
  - "Which features drive highest usage/satisfaction?"

- **Data Sources:**
  - Internal: Customer feedback database, support tickets, usage analytics
  - External: Competitive feature analysis, market research
  - Primary: Customer interviews, advisory board feedback

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Complete analysis plan (high-level is fine)
- ‚ùå All data gathered
- ‚ùå Final analysis questions (these can evolve)
- ‚ùå Statistical study design

---

### 4. Root Cause Investigation Path ‚úì

- [ ] **Root causes theorized (not proven)**
  - Apparent root causes identified for each major branch
  - Multiple potential causes considered
  - Surface causes vs. deeper drivers distinguished
  - Causal mechanisms explained (why does this cause churn?)

- [ ] **Assumptions about root causes documented**
  - What we believe to be true (without proof)
  - Why we believe it (logic, preliminary evidence, pattern)
  - What evidence would prove/disprove it
  - Risk if assumption is wrong

- [ ] **Root cause relationships mapped**
  - How different root causes interact
  - Primary vs. secondary causes identified
  - Feedback loops noted (if any)
  - Leverage points identified (where to focus fix efforts)

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Primary Root Cause:** Competitor X launched feature Y that matches customer need better than our solution
  - **Secondary Root Causes:** We haven't communicated our roadmap; we haven't invested in that feature area
  - **Leverage Point:** Either develop competitive feature OR significantly improve communications about differentiation
  - **Evidence Needed:** Customer preference research, competitive analysis, roadmap review

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Proven root causes
- ‚ùå Quantified impact of each root cause
- ‚ùå Complete fishbone/cause-effect diagrams
- ‚ùå Five-whys analysis (though helpful)

---

### 5. Strategic Coherence ‚úì

- [ ] **Decomposition connects back to original problem**
  - All components together explain the full problem
  - No major aspect of original problem left unexplored
  - Scope hasn't drifted
  - Original success criteria still relevant

- [ ] **Specialist approach confirmed**
  - Systematic methodology chosen for this problem
  - Framework choices justified
  - Flexibility built in for emergent findings
  - Next phase (ANALYSE) will have clear direction

- [ ] **Stakeholder perspectives incorporated**
  - Different stakeholder views on root causes considered
  - Conflicting perspectives noted
  - Whose perspective will be validated first?
  - Communication plan for findings in place

**What This Looks Like:**
- Decomposition directly addresses original problem: "Why are we losing customers?"
- Not exploring: "How should we reorganize sales?" (different problem)
- Specialist approach: Systematic decomposition ‚Üí hypothesis testing ‚Üí root cause validation
- Multiple perspectives: CEO thinks competition; Sales thinks product; Product thinks marketing

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Complete stakeholder agreement
- ‚ùå Resolved perspective conflicts
- ‚ùå Final answer on whose perspective is correct

---

### 6. Documentation & Handoff ‚úì

- [ ] **Problem structure document created**
  - Issue tree or equivalent visualization
  - Component descriptions
  - Relationships explained
  - Component prioritization clear

- [ ] **Hypothesis document prepared**
  - All hypotheses listed
  - Each with testing approach
  - Prioritized by impact and effort
  - Clear validation criteria for each

- [ ] **Analysis work plan documented**
  - Analysis tasks identified
  - Sequence and dependencies clear
  - Resource requirements noted
  - Data sources and feasibility assessed

- [ ] **Persona Handoff created**
  - Problem structure summary
  - Key hypotheses to test
  - Analysis questions for Analyst
  - Data/resources available
  - Interdependencies noted
  - Risk factors from Specialist perspective

**What This Looks Like:**
- Problem Structure: 1-page visual tree showing decomposition
- Hypothesis Doc: 2-3 pages listing hypotheses, tests, validation criteria
- Analysis Plan: 1-2 pages showing what analyses are needed and order
- Handoff: 1-page summary of Specialist's work and handoff to Analyst

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Polished visualizations
- ‚ùå Complete analysis specifications
- ‚ùå Final data (just sources identified)
- ‚ùå Presentation-ready documents

---

## Enhancing Criteria (Improving Quality)

These items strengthen the phase but aren't strictly blocking:

- [ ] **Multiple hypotheses considered for each branch**
  - At least 2-3 alternative explanations explored
  - Why most likely hypothesis was selected explained
  - Scenarios where alternatives might be true identified

- [ ] **Quick-win analysis identified**
  - Low-effort hypotheses that could be tested quickly
  - Preliminary interviews or data analysis suggested
  - Early findings that inform later analysis noted

- [ ] **Cross-functional perspectives explicitly gathered**
  - Different departments' views on root causes captured
  - Potential sources of resistance identified
  - Assumptions that different teams hold noted

- [ ] **Constraint analysis completed**
  - Time constraints for investigating identified
  - Resource constraints noted
  - Political/organizational constraints surfaced
  - Analysis approach adapted to constraints

- [ ] **Communication strategy outlined**
  - How findings will be presented to different audiences
  - Potential sensitivities anticipated
  - Key messages for each stakeholder considered

---

## Quality Checks (Before Handoff)

Before confirming phase completion, ask yourself:

1. **Will the Analyst understand what to analyze?**
   - Are components clearly defined?
   - Are hypotheses clear?
   - Will Analyst know what to look for?

2. **Is the analysis realistic and feasible?**
   - Can this be analyzed in reasonable timeframe?
   - Is data available or obtainable?
   - Are resources adequate?

3. **Will analysis provide decision-making insight?**
   - Does problem decomposition surface root causes?
   - Will hypothesis testing answer key questions?
   - Can results inform strategic decisions?

4. **Does the Specialist feel confident about the structure?**
   - Have they explored the problem thoroughly?
   - Do they feel good about the decomposition?
   - Are they ready to hand off?

---

## Readiness Assessment

### ‚úÖ Ready to Proceed to ANALYSE When

All blocking criteria are met:
- Problem is decomposed into logical, analyzable components
- Hypotheses are formulated with testing approaches
- Analysis framework is clear and sequenced
- Root causes are theorized and documented
- Strategic coherence is maintained
- Documentation is complete and handed off

**The Analyst will have a clear road map for systematic investigation.**

---

### üîÑ Needs More Work When

One or more blocking criteria are unmet:

- **Decomposition feels incomplete?**
  - ‚Üí Use problem-structuring task to refine
  - ‚Üí Add missing branches
  - ‚Üí Test MECE principle

- **Hypotheses unclear?**
  - ‚Üí Use hypothesis-testing task framework
  - ‚Üí Write If/Then statements
  - ‚Üí Define validation criteria

- **Analysis approach undefined?**
  - ‚Üí Identify what analyses are needed
  - ‚Üí Sequence them logically
  - ‚Üí Estimate effort and feasibility

- **Root causes not theorized?**
  - ‚Üí Use root-cause-analysis task
  - ‚Üí Consider multiple perspectives
  - ‚Üí Distinguish likely from possible causes

---

## What This Phase DOES Include

‚úÖ Problem decomposition (MECE structure)
‚úÖ Hypothesis formation and prioritization
‚úÖ Testable hypotheses with validation criteria
‚úÖ Root cause theories (not yet proven)
‚úÖ Analysis work plan
‚úÖ Key investigation questions
‚úÖ Data gaps identified

---

## What This Phase DOES NOT Include

‚ùå Analysis or testing of hypotheses (that's ANALYSE)
‚ùå Definitive root cause identification (that's ANALYSE)
‚ùå Market research or competitive analysis (that's ANALYSE)
‚ùå Pattern recognition (that's ANALYSE)
‚ùå Solution recommendations (that's DECIDE)
‚ùå Implementation planning (that's ACT)

---

## Common Blockers & How to Resolve

| Blocker | Signal | Resolution |
|---------|--------|-----------|
| **Decomposition not MECE** | Overlapping or missing categories | Use problem-structuring task; test with "does this cover everything uniquely?" |
| **Too many hypotheses** | List has 10+ items for one branch | Consolidate; focus on most impactful |
| **Hypotheses not testable** | "Customers are unhappy" | Reframe: "What specific pain point causes churn?" |
| **Analysis plan unrealistic** | "Need 6 months of data gathering" | Scope down; identify critical path items |
| **No data identified** | "We don't have this information" | Identify proxy data; plan interviews; make assumptions explicit |
| **Scope creeping** | Decomposition going into new areas | Return to original problem; stay focused |

---

## Post-Completion Actions

Once this checklist passes:

1. **Create Problem Structure Document**
   - Use `problem-structuring.md` task as reference
   - Document issue tree or equivalent
   - Make visual and clear

2. **Create Hypothesis Document**
   - Use `hypothesis-testing.md` task as reference
   - List all hypotheses
   - Include testing approaches and validation criteria

3. **Create Analysis Work Plan**
   - Identify all analyses needed
   - Sequence them
   - Estimate effort/resources

4. **Prepare Persona Handoff**
   - Use `persona-handoff-template.md`
   - Summarize problem structure
   - Highlight key hypotheses for testing
   - Provide analysis work plan

5. **Hand off to Strategic Analyst**
   - Share all decomposition documents
   - Share analysis work plan
   - Confirm Analyst ready to proceed
   - Load ANALYSE phase files

6. **Archive SPLIT Materials**
   - Save all work
   - Reference for future phases
   - Keep accessible

---

## Notes & Observations

Use this space to capture phase-specific insights:

- **What worked well in this phase?**

- **What was challenging?**

- **Unexpected insights about the problem?**

- **For future engagements:**

---

## Sign-Off

**Phase Completed By:** __________________ (Strategic Specialist)

**Date Completed:** __________________

**Confirmed Ready for ANALYSE:** ‚òê Yes ‚òê No

**If No, specific blockers:**

---

## Related Resources

- **Task:** `tasks/problem-structuring.md`
- **Task:** `tasks/hypothesis-testing.md`
- **Task:** `tasks/root-cause-analysis.md`
- **Framework Reference:** `data/00_strategic-frameworks.md` (Split section)
- **Output Template:** `templates/step-context-brief-template.md`
- **Handoff Template:** `templates/persona-handoff-template.md`

==================== START: stakeholder-map-validation-checklist ====================
# Stakeholder Map Validation Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that a completed Stakeholder Map identifies all key stakeholders, assesses their interests and influence, and outlines engagement strategy for alignment and buy-in.

## What Gets Validated

**Template Reference:** `templates/stakeholder-map.md`

**Used In:** All phases for stakeholder management and alignment

**Audience:** Strategy team, project leaders, communication teams

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. Stakeholders Are Comprehensively Identified ‚úì

- [ ] **All key stakeholder groups identified**
  - Decision makers (who decides?)
  - Influencers (who shapes thinking?)
  - Implementers (who makes it happen?)
  - Affected parties (who is impacted?)
  - Blockers/resisters (who might oppose?)

- [ ] **Stakeholders described clearly**
  - Role and title
  - Department/function
  - Decision authority (if applicable)
  - Level of engagement to date

- [ ] **Identification is comprehensive**
  - Would this catch resistance?
  - Are hidden influencers identified?
  - Are blockers named explicitly?
  - Is coverage complete?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
DECISION MAKERS:
- CEO (Strategic direction authority)
- CFO (Budget/investment approval)
- Board of Directors (If capital decision)

INFLUENCERS:
- VP Product (Product strategy perspective)
- VP Sales (GTM strategy perspective)
- Head of Customer Success (Customer perspective)

IMPLEMENTERS:
- VP Product (Product roadmap execution)
- VP Sales (GTM execution)
- Engineering Lead (Product development)
- Finance Director (Budgeting and tracking)

AFFECTED PARTIES:
- Sales team (New go-to-market model)
- Product team (Dual product focus)
- Customer success team (New segment support model)
- Enterprise customers (Organization focus)

POTENTIAL RESISTERS:
- VP Product (Prefers single product focus)
- Some enterprise customers (Want company to stay focused)
- Engineering (Resource constraints)
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Every employee identified
- ‚ùå Complete organizational chart
- ‚ùå Detailed role descriptions
- ‚ùå All potential blockers (main ones sufficient)

---

### 2. Stakeholder Interests & Positions Are Clear ‚úì

- [ ] **Each stakeholder's primary interests understood**
  - What does this person care about?
  - What are their concerns?
  - What would they gain/lose?
  - What are their constraints?

- [ ] **Current position is assessed**
  - Are they supportive, neutral, or opposed?
  - Why are they in this position?
  - What would move them?
  - How strong is their position?

- [ ] **Sources of information captured**
  - How do we know their position?
  - Who told us? When?
  - How confident are we in this assessment?
  - Have we confirmed directly?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
STAKEHOLDER: CEO

Primary Interests:
- Company growth and profitability
- Competitive positioning
- Risk management
- Board confidence

Position: INTERESTED BUT CAUTIOUS
- Sees SMB opportunity as strategic
- Concerned about organizational distraction
- Wants data-driven decision
- Wants clear execution plan before committing

What would gain: Clear path to $40M+ revenue by Year 3
What could lose: Enterprise focus and profitability if execution fails
Constraints: Limited management bandwidth; quarterly planning priorities
Move toward support: Data showing SMB is viable, execution roadmap clear

Source: Direct conversation during discovery

---

STAKEHOLDER: VP Sales

Primary Interests:
- Sales growth and quota achievement
- Team capability and morale
- Commission structure and comp
- Easy-to-win opportunities

Position: STRONGLY SUPPORTIVE
- SMB market represents new opportunity
- Frustrated with losing SMB deals to cheaper competitors
- Sees dual-segment as growth opportunity
- Wants to start immediately

What would gain: New market segment with growth potential; new comp opportunity
What could lose: If SMB takes resources, enterprise growth might slow
Constraints: Limited team capacity; training needs for SMB motion
Move toward alignment: Ensure enterprise team stays resourced and supported

Source: Multiple conversations; strong conviction evident

---

STAKEHOLDER: VP Product

Primary Interests:
- Product quality and simplicity
- Engineering team focus
- Product-market fit
- Technical leadership

Position: HESITANT/SKEPTICAL
- Concerned about product complexity from dual strategy
- Worried about R&D focus being split
- Questions whether we can do both well
- Prefers staying enterprise-only

What would gain: If we prove simple SMB product possible, becomes believer
What could lose: Product simplicity and focus if badly executed
Constraints: Engineering capacity limited (10 engineers); current roadmap full
Move toward support: Clear product strategy for SMB, separate team structure

Source: Team meetings and one-on-one conversations; expressed concerns
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Every stakeholder's complete perspective
- ‚ùå Detailed psychographic analysis
- ‚ùå Perfect accuracy in position (working assessment ok)
- ‚ùå Consensus on positions

---

### 3. Influence & Power Assessed ‚úì

- [ ] **Influence is mapped clearly**
  - Who has formal authority?
  - Who has informal influence?
  - Who would change others' minds?
  - Who can block decisions?

- [ ] **Power dynamics understood**
  - Who decides what?
  - Who influences the decision-maker?
  - Are there coalitions or factions?
  - Who is most critical to success?

- [ ] **Stakeholder matrix created**
  - High power, high interest (manage closely)
  - High power, low interest (keep satisfied)
  - Low power, high interest (keep informed)
  - Low power, low interest (monitor)

**What This Looks Like:**
```
STAKEHOLDER INFLUENCE MATRIX:

HIGH POWER / HIGH INTEREST (Manage Closely):
- CEO (Decision authority, strategic interest)
- CFO (Budget authority, financial interest)
- VP Product (Implementation authority, technical concerns)
- VP Sales (Implementation authority, market interest)

HIGH POWER / LOW INTEREST (Keep Satisfied):
- Board of Directors (Governance, financial returns)
- COO (Organizational impact, if exists)

LOW POWER / HIGH INTEREST (Keep Informed):
- Customer Success team (Implementation, customer impact)
- Sales team (Execution, career impact)
- Engineering team (Implementation, workload)

LOW POWER / LOW INTEREST (Monitor):
- Support team (Indirect impact)
- Marketing team (Dependent on decision)

CRITICAL STAKEHOLDERS:
- CEO: Can kill or approve decision
- CFO: Controls investment funding
- VP Product: Controls product direction and engineering
- VP Sales: Controls GTM execution
- Enterprise customer advisory board: Can block through dissatisfaction

COALITIONS:
- Growth coalition: CEO + VP Sales + CFO (if ROI clear)
  Supports SMB entry as growth opportunity

- Conservative coalition: VP Product + some enterprise customers
  Prefers enterprise focus; concerned about distraction
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Detailed influence network analysis
- ‚ùå Quantified power scores
- ‚ùå Complete coalition mapping
- ‚ùå Hidden relationship charts

---

### 4. Engagement Strategy Is Defined ‚úì

- [ ] **For each key stakeholder, engagement approach defined**
  - What information do they need?
  - How and when should they be engaged?
  - Who should engage with them?
  - What's the goal of engagement?

- [ ] **For blockers/resisters, strategy addresses concerns**
  - What would move them?
  - How do we address their concerns?
  - Do we need to include them in solution design?
  - Can we make them at least neutral?

- [ ] **Communication approach is tailored**
  - Different stakeholders need different info
  - Timing matters (when to engage)
  - Channel matters (who delivers message)
  - Frequency matters (cadence of engagement)

**What This Looks Like:**
```
ENGAGEMENT STRATEGY:

STAKEHOLDER: CEO

Information Needed:
- Market opportunity validation (TAM/SAM/SOM)
- Financial viability (ROI, payback period)
- Execution risk and mitigations
- Competitive threat and timing

Engagement Approach:
- Monthly 1-on-1 updates during analysis phase
- Present comprehensive brief at phase completion
- Facilitate executive decision meeting
- Regular steering committee updates during execution

Who Engages:
- Strategy lead (owns communication)
- CEO comfort: Direct conversation preferred

Goal: Secure CEO approval and active sponsorship

---

STAKEHOLDER: VP Product (Resister/Skeptic)

Information Needed:
- Product strategy for SMB (simple ‚â† dumbed down)
- How we protect enterprise product excellence
- Organizational/team structure for dual focus
- Resource plan and constraints

Engagement Approach:
- Early 1-on-1 to understand concerns (don't wait)
- Involve in product strategy design (include vs. resist)
- Include in analysis of options
- Present recommendation with clear product approach
- Offer collaboration on solution design

Who Engages:
- Chief Product Officer (peer engagement)
- Strategy lead (include in working sessions)

Goal: Move from skeptic to supporter (or at least neutral)
Key insight: Blocking usually from concern, not opposition.
Address concerns and can move person toward alignment.

---

STAKEHOLDER: Sales team (Implementers)

Information Needed:
- SMB market opportunity and timeline
- Go-to-market approach
- Changes to their roles/comp
- Support and training available

Engagement Approach:
- Early communication (anticipate concerns)
- Involve in market research (their input valuable)
- Clear timeline and milestones
- Regular updates on progress
- Training and enablement plan

Who Engages:
- VP Sales (direct leadership)
- Strategy team (decision context)

Goal: Build enthusiasm and readiness for execution

---

STAKEHOLDER: Enterprise customers

Information Needed:
- Will company stay focused on enterprise?
- How will service/support be impacted?
- Any pricing/contract changes?
- How to be part of decision if desired

Engagement Approach:
- Proactive communication (don't let rumors start)
- Customer advisory board input (if applicable)
- Message: Enterprise remains core focus
- Show clear strategy for SMB that supports enterprise
- Solicit feedback and address concerns

Who Engages:
- Chief Customer Officer or VP CS
- CEO (for key customers if needed)

Goal: Maintain customer confidence and loyalty
Risk: Customers worried about distraction could churn
Mitigation: Early, honest communication
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Individual engagement plans for every employee
- ‚ùå Complete change management program
- ‚ùå Detailed communication calendar
- ‚ùå Scripts or talking points

---

### 5. Alignment Gaps & Conflicts Identified ‚úì

- [ ] **Stakeholder conflicts surfaced**
  - Where do stakeholders disagree?
  - What's driving the disagreement?
  - How significant is the conflict?
  - Can conflict be resolved?

- [ ] **Misaligned perspectives noted**
  - Where might stakeholders misunderstand strategy?
  - Are there hidden objections?
  - Do stakeholders understand each other's concerns?
  - Could misalignment emerge later?

- [ ] **Strategy for alignment addressed**
  - How do we build consensus?
  - Where do we need compromise?
  - Where do we need education?
  - What's non-negotiable?

**What This Looks Like:**
```
STAKEHOLDER CONFLICTS:

Conflict 1: Enterprise vs. SMB Focus

VP Product wants: Continue enterprise-only focus
VP Sales wants: Pursue SMB opportunity immediately
CEO wants: Data-driven decision with clear execution plan
CFO wants: Strategy that maximizes ROI

Gap: Different views on market opportunity and execution capability

Resolution approach:
- Present data on both markets
- Show execution plan addresses resource concerns
- Propose separate teams (addresses focus concern)
- Model financials for both scenarios
- Empower CEO to make decision with full information

---

Conflict 2: Speed vs. Caution

VP Sales wants: Launch SMB product ASAP (fear of competition)
VP Product wants: Careful, deliberate approach (quality concern)
CEO wants: Fast enough to capture opportunity, slow enough to get right

Gap: Different risk tolerance and time horizons

Resolution approach:
- Acknowledge both concerns are valid
- Define phased approach (MVP launch in 6 months, scale from there)
- Build in quality gates but maintain aggressive timeline
- Regular reviews to assess execution quality

---

MISALIGNMENT RISKS:

Risk 1: Sales team assumes SMB launch will be quick
- Reality: Product development takes 6+ months
- Mitigation: Set expectations early; show timeline; manage surprises

Risk 2: Enterprise customers fear company will abandon enterprise
- Reality: Enterprise is core but we're also pursuing SMB
- Mitigation: Clear messaging that enterprise remains priority

Risk 3: VP Product assumes SMB will distract from enterprise
- Reality: Separate teams and roadmaps can prevent distraction
- Mitigation: Clear organizational structure and resource allocation
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Every possible conflict identified
- ‚ùå Detailed conflict resolution strategy
- ‚ùå Consensus on resolutions
- ‚ùå Complete alignment guarantee

---

### 6. Organization & Documentation ‚úì

- [ ] **Map is clear and easy to understand**
  - Stakeholder positions visible at a glance
  - Influence dynamics obvious
  - Engagement strategy clear
  - Could be shared with leadership

- [ ] **Supporting narrative is complete**
  - Stakeholder descriptions clear
  - Interests and positions explained
  - Conflicts and gaps identified
  - Engagement strategy articulated

- [ ] **Professional quality**
  - Well-organized
  - Grammar and spelling correct
  - Clear formatting
  - Appropriate tone

**What This Looks Like:**
```
STRUCTURE:

1. Stakeholder Summary Table
   - All stakeholders listed
   - Role/title
   - Position (support/neutral/oppose)
   - Influence level
   - Key interest

2. Stakeholder Influence Matrix (Visual)
   - 2x2 matrix showing power vs. interest
   - Stakeholders plotted
   - Engagement approach by quadrant

3. Detailed Stakeholder Profiles
   - For key stakeholders: interests, position, move strategy

4. Stakeholder Alignment Assessment
   - Where is consensus?
   - Where are conflicts?
   - What's the alignment risk?
   - Strategy for building alignment

5. Engagement Plan
   - By stakeholder or stakeholder group
   - What info they need
   - How/when to engage
   - Who engages
   - What's the goal

6. Risk Assessment
   - What stakeholder actions could jeopardize decision?
   - How likely are risks?
   - What's the mitigation strategy?
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Beautiful visual design
- ‚ùå Complex influence network graphs
- ‚ùå Detailed change management plan
- ‚ùå Individual coaching plans

---

## Enhancing Criteria (Improving Quality)

These items strengthen the map but aren't strictly blocking:

- [ ] **Stakeholder profiles are rich**
  - Background and history captured
  - Personality and style noted
  - Personal interests and motivations visible
  - What they care about beyond this issue

- [ ] **Communication preferences documented**
  - How does each person prefer to communicate?
  - What's their decision-making style?
  - What information do they trust most?
  - How do they respond to data vs. narrative?

- [ ] **Coalition building strategy**
  - Who could partner with whom?
  - Are there natural allies?
  - Could diverse coalitions emerge?
  - How to build winning coalition?

- [ ] **Contingency for unexpected opposition**
  - What if key stakeholder opposes?
  - How would we respond?
  - What's our fallback position?
  - Can we proceed without their support?

---

## Quality Checks

Before confirming map is complete, ask yourself:

1. **Would this identify problems early?**
   - Would we catch blocker/resister?
   - Would we understand resistance?
   - Would engagement strategy address it?
   - Would we have time to respond?

2. **Is stakeholder assessment credible?**
   - Based on real conversation or assumption?
   - Would stakeholders recognize their positions?
   - Are concerns fairly represented?
   - Is there bias in assessment?

3. **Is engagement strategy realistic?**
   - Can we actually engage this way?
   - Do we have time/resources?
   - Are approaches appropriate?
   - Would they actually move stakeholders?

4. **Would this support alignment?**
   - Does it show where consensus exists?
   - Does it identify conflicts?
   - Does strategy address conflicts?
   - Would execution follow this plan?

---

## Readiness Assessment

### ‚úÖ Map is Ready When

All blocking criteria are met:
- Stakeholders are comprehensively identified
- Interests and positions are clear
- Influence and power are assessed
- Engagement strategy is defined
- Alignment gaps and conflicts identified
- Organization and documentation are good

**Map can guide stakeholder alignment efforts.**

---

## Common Issues & Resolution

| Issue | Signal | Resolution |
|-------|--------|-----------|
| **Too many stakeholders** | "50 people listed" | Focus on key influencers; group others |
| **Positions unclear** | "Don't know if they support" | Assess based on prior interactions or ask directly |
| **No engagement plan** | "How do we engage them?" | Define specific information needs and approaches |
| **Conflicts missing** | "This seems unanimous" | Look deeper; identify hidden concerns |
| **Influence underestimated** | "Surprise opposition later" | Identify all people who can influence decision |
| **Too theoretical** | "Doesn't feel practical" | Ground in real stakeholder dynamics |

---

## Post-Validation Actions

Once this checklist passes:

1. **Distribute Map to Leadership**
   - Share with CEO/decision-maker
   - Share with communication lead
   - Confirm understanding of stakeholder landscape
   - Adjust if needed based on feedback

2. **Execute Engagement Strategy**
   - Begin stakeholder engagements
   - Track stakeholder positions
   - Update map as positions evolve
   - Adjust approach if needed

3. **Monitor Alignment Progress**
   - Track movement toward consensus
   - Identify emerging conflicts
   - Celebrate early wins/conversions
   - Address new concerns

4. **Prepare for Decision**
   - Assess readiness for decision meeting
   - Gauge support/opposition
   - Address last-minute concerns
   - Plan communication after decision

5. **Archive & Reference**
   - Save stakeholder map
   - Document engagement results
   - Note what worked/didn't work
   - Reference for implementation phase

---

==================== START: story-phase-completion-checklist ====================
# STORY Phase Completion Checklist

## Purpose

Validate that the STORY phase (Strategic Communicator) has completed all essential work before transitioning to the DECIDE phase. This checklist ensures strategic insights have been transformed into compelling narratives that inform and influence stakeholder thinking about critical strategic decisions.

## What This Phase Accomplishes

The STORY phase makes strategic insights accessible and persuasive. The Strategic Communicator ensures:
- Complex analysis becomes compelling narrative
- Insights are tailored to different stakeholders
- Case for action is compelling
- Key messages are consistent across audiences
- Foundation for decision-making is solid

## Blocking Criteria (All Required)

### 1. Core Strategic Narrative Developed ‚úì

- [ ] **Master narrative created**
  - Clear story arc (current state ‚Üí challenge ‚Üí analysis ‚Üí insight ‚Üí choice point)
  - Core message repeated throughout
  - Evidence woven into story (not appended as separate analysis)
  - Emotional resonance with audience
  - Call-to-action (what decision/action is being informed)

- [ ] **Narrative logic is clear**
  - Each element builds on previous
  - Why we did certain analyses is clear
  - Why certain findings matter is explained
  - Implications are front-and-center (not buried)
  - Path to decision is visible

- [ ] **Narrative is evidence-based**
  - Claims are supported by findings
  - Supporting data provided
  - Caveats and uncertainties acknowledged
  - Tone is credible (not overselling)

**What This Looks Like:**
```
NARRATIVE ARC:
Current State: Enterprise success, SMB challenges
Challenge: Market opportunity vs. resource constraints
Analysis: Deep dive into churn, competition, opportunity
Insight: Double-sided growth opportunity (enterprise + SMB)
Choice Point: Do we defend premium or expand downmarket?
Call-to-Action: Strategic decision needed by [date]
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect storytelling
- ‚ùå Polished presentation
- ‚ùå Unanimous agreement with narrative
- ‚ùå Final decision on what to do

---

### 2. Stakeholder Narratives Customized ‚úì

- [ ] **Key stakeholder groups identified**
  - Executive leadership
  - Board of directors (if relevant)
  - Operational leadership (Sales, Product, Ops)
  - Affected teams/departments
  - External stakeholders (if relevant)

- [ ] **Customized narratives for each group**
  - For executives: Strategic implications and business impact
  - For operations: What this means for their areas, what changes
  - For board: Market opportunity, competitive position, risk management
  - For affected teams: How they're impacted, what they need to do
  - For external: Opportunity/threat relevant to their interests

- [ ] **Core message is consistent across audiences**
  - Different narratives tell same basic story
  - Supporting evidence is consistent
  - Tone is appropriate for each audience
  - No contradictions between narratives

**What This Looks Like:**
- **For CEO:** "Strategic choice between defending premium positioning or capturing growing SMB market; decision affects 3-year roadmap"
- **For Sales:** "Competitor moving into SMB segment aggressively; we're at risk of losing mid-market customers; strategic response being formulated"
- **For Product:** "Analysis shows feature gaps vs. competitors; two possible strategic responses (premium features for enterprise OR simplified feature set for SMB); strategic direction needed"
- **For Board:** "Market analysis shows $500M opportunity in adjacent segment; current strategy captures enterprise (stable, profitable); opportunity to expand total addressable market"

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Perfect tailoring for every individual
- ‚ùå Handling of all possible stakeholder concerns
- ‚ùå Comprehensive internal communication plan
- ‚ùå Defined messaging hierarchy

---

### 3. Key Messages & Messaging Framework ‚úì

- [ ] **Core key messages defined (3-5 primary)**
  - Each message is simple (1-2 sentences max)
  - Each message is memorable
  - Messages are consistent across narratives
  - Messages are backed by evidence
  - Messages point toward decision/action

- [ ] **Message architecture built**
  - Primary message (the headline)
  - Supporting messages (evidence/reasoning)
  - Alternative perspectives acknowledged
  - Counterarguments addressed
  - Call-to-action clear

- [ ] **Supporting evidence for each message**
  - Data points supporting each message
  - Real quotes or examples (if available)
  - Visualizations supporting key points
  - Confidence levels transparent

**What This Looks Like:**
```
PRIMARY MESSAGE:
"We have a strategic choice: focus exclusively on profitable
enterprise market OR expand into underserved SMB segment"

SUPPORTING MESSAGES:
1. "Enterprise is stable and highly profitable ($15M ARR, 95% retention)"
2. "SMB segment is in crisis (40% annual churn, $5M ARR at risk)"
3. "Market data shows SMB segment is large ($2B) and growing 25% annually"
4. "Competitors are moving downmarket aggressively"
5. "We can serve both with different product/pricing models"

EVIDENCE:
- Financial: ARR by segment, retention by segment
- Market: TAM analysis, competitor positioning
- Customer: Churn analysis, NPS by segment
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Every possible supporting data point
- ‚ùå Perfect message wording
- ‚ùå Unanimous stakeholder agreement
- ‚ùå Final positioning statement

---

### 4. Executive Communication Ready ‚úì

- [ ] **Executive summary/brief prepared**
  - 2-3 page document (maximum)
  - Situation, findings, implications stated
  - Strategic choice articulated
  - Recommendations or questions for decision
  - Next steps clear

- [ ] **Presentation structure planned**
  - Opening that engages
  - Problem/opportunity clearly set up
  - Evidence presented logically
  - Implications explained
  - Decision points/options outlined
  - Call-to-action clear
  - Q&A preparation (likely questions anticipated)

- [ ] **Visuals planned**
  - Key charts/visuals identified
  - Data visualization strategy
  - Not too many (focus on key points)
  - Visuals tell story (not just pretty)

**What This Looks Like:**
- **2-page Brief:**
  - Page 1: Situation, challenge, key findings
  - Page 2: Implications, strategic choice, next steps

- **15-minute Presentation:**
  - Opening (30 sec): Business situation
  - Problem (2 min): What's happening with churn
  - Analysis (5 min): Why it's happening
  - Insight (4 min): What it means strategically
  - Choice (2 min): What decision needs to be made
  - Path Forward (1.5 min): What we do next

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Polished PowerPoint
- ‚ùå Complete presentation (outline/script sufficient)
- ‚ùå Every possible visual
- ‚ùå Perfect timing

---

### 5. Alternative Perspectives Addressed ‚úì

- [ ] **Different viewpoints acknowledged**
  - "Some might argue..." perspectives identified
  - Why different stakeholders might see this differently
  - Legitimate concerns surfaced
  - Not dismissed or minimized

- [ ] **Counterarguments addressed**
  - What would challenge our narrative?
  - How do we respond to "but what about...?"
  - Weaknesses in our argument acknowledged
  - What would prove us wrong identified

- [ ] **Uncertainty is transparent**
  - What we're confident about stated
  - What we're less certain about identified
  - What could change our mind noted
  - Risk factors acknowledged

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Alternative View 1:** "Maybe SMB churn is temporary and will stabilize"
  - **Response:** "Possible, but trend data shows continued decline; competitor pressure increasing"

- **Alternative View 2:** "Maybe we should just wait and see what happens"
  - **Response:** "Market window may close; competitors moving fast; window of opportunity may be 6-12 months"

- **Uncertainty:** "We're confident about churn drivers; less certain about exact market sizing; would validate through customer research before committing resources"

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Every possible objection addressed
- ‚ùå Consensus on alternative views
- ‚ùå Complete risk mitigation plans
- ‚ùå Resolved uncertainties

---

### 6. Decision Framework for Next Phase ‚úì

- [ ] **Decision points are explicit**
  - What decision(s) need to be made?
  - Who needs to decide?
  - What's the timeline for decision?
  - What information/input is needed for decision?

- [ ] **Decision options are outlined**
  - Option 1 (and implications)
  - Option 2 (and implications)
  - Option 3 if relevant (and implications)
  - What each option would mean for organization/customers/strategy

- [ ] **Criteria for decision are suggested**
  - What factors should inform decision?
  - Market opportunity vs. resource constraints
  - Competitive timing
  - Organizational capability
  - Financial implications

**What This Looks Like:**
```
DECISION: Should we expand to SMB segment?

OPTIONS:
Option 1: Focus exclusively on enterprise
  - Keep current positioning and pricing
  - Implications: Miss $500M market opportunity; defend against competitive downmarket moves

Option 2: Create separate SMB offering
  - New product, pricing, go-to-market
  - Implications: Double R&D effort; new GTM complexity; open two-sided growth

Option 3: Acquire SMB-focused competitor
  - Faster entry; built-in product
  - Implications: Integration risk; management distraction; higher investment

DECISION CRITERIA:
- Market opportunity size and timeline
- Competitive threat timeline
- Resource availability
- Organizational appetite for dual strategies
- Financial ROI/payback
```

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Recommendation (that's DECIDE phase)
- ‚ùå Detailed business cases (that's DECIDE)
- ‚ùå Final decision (that's executive decision-making)
- ‚ùå Implementation implications (that's ACT)

---

### 7. Documentation & Handoff ‚úì

- [ ] **Strategic narrative document created**
  - Story arc clear
  - Evidence woven in
  - Implications emphasized
  - Decision points articulated
  - 5-10 pages (enough detail to stand alone)

- [ ] **Stakeholder-specific narratives prepared**
  - Executive version (2-3 pages)
  - Operational leadership version (3-4 pages)
  - Board version (if relevant)
  - Team communication version
  - All aligned in core message

- [ ] **Supporting materials compiled**
  - Key charts and visuals
  - Detailed findings reference
  - Message framework document
  - Presentation outline/script

- [ ] **Persona Handoff created**
  - Narrative summary
  - Key decision points
  - Strategic options outlined
  - Questions/concerns for Advisor to address in DECIDE
  - Stakeholder perspectives documented
  - Execution considerations noted

**What This Looks Like:**
- **Narrative Document:** 8-10 page strategic brief with story arc, findings, implications
- **Executive Brief:** 2-3 page summary for busy executives
- **Presentation Outline:** 15-20 minute presentation script with speaker notes
- **Message Framework:** Document with primary message, supporting messages, evidence

**What This Does NOT Require:**
- ‚ùå Polished presentations
- ‚ùå Complete stakeholder communication plan
- ‚ùå Final marketing/communications materials
- ‚ùå Resolved stakeholder concerns

---

## Enhancing Criteria (Improving Quality)

These items strengthen the phase but aren't strictly blocking:

- [ ] **Story tested with key stakeholders**
  - Narrative reviewed with sample of stakeholders
  - Feedback incorporated
  - Resonance assessed
  - Concerns surfaced and addressed

- [ ] **Compelling evidence compilation**
  - Customer stories/quotes included
  - Competitive examples cited
  - Market trend examples provided
  - Emotional resonance created through examples

- [ ] **Visual storyline developed**
  - Charts that tell the story
  - Flow from one visual to next
  - Key insights emphasized visually
  - Professional quality (not required, but helpful)

- [ ] **Presentation rehearsed**
  - Timing verified
  - Likely questions anticipated
  - Transitions smooth
  - Spokesperson confident

- [ ] **Organizational readiness assessed**
  - How will different groups receive this?
  - Are there sensitivities to navigate?
  - Is there organizational capacity for recommended changes?
  - Communication sequencing identified

---

## Quality Checks (Before Handoff)

Before confirming phase completion, ask yourself:

1. **Is the narrative truly compelling?**
   - Would it move someone to action?
   - Does it resonate emotionally as well as intellectually?
   - Does it make the case for why this matters?
   - Would different stakeholders find it persuasive?

2. **Is the story clear without the analysis?**
   - Could someone understand the logic without detailed data?
   - Do they see why analysis was conducted?
   - Do implications flow logically from findings?
   - Is path to decision clear?

3. **Are stakeholders adequately addressed?**
   - Would each key group understand what this means for them?
   - Are their concerns/perspectives represented?
   - Would they feel heard and understood?
   - Would they be ready to engage in decision?

4. **Does the Communicator feel the story is ready?**
   - Are they confident in the narrative?
   - Can they answer questions about findings?
   - Are they ready to hand off to Advisor?
   - Do they feel the story is compelling?

---

## Readiness Assessment

### ‚úÖ Ready to Proceed to DECIDE When

All blocking criteria are met:
- Core narrative is developed with clear story arc
- Stakeholder narratives are customized and consistent
- Key messages are defined and supported
- Executive communication is prepared
- Alternative perspectives are addressed
- Decision framework is outlined
- Documentation is complete and handed off

**The Advisor will have solid narrative foundation to facilitate high-quality decisions.**

---

### üîÑ Needs More Work When

One or more blocking criteria are unmet:

- **Narrative not compelling?**
  - ‚Üí Add more specificity/examples
  - ‚Üí Clarify emotional resonance
  - ‚Üí Strengthen connection to stakeholder concerns

- **Stakeholder needs unclear?**
  - ‚Üí Identify what each stakeholder cares about
  - ‚Üí Clarify what changes for each
  - ‚Üí Customize messaging

- **Messages too many or unclear?**
  - ‚Üí Consolidate to 3-5 core messages
  - ‚Üí Make each simple and memorable
  - ‚Üí Ensure evidence supports each

- **Executive communication weak?**
  - ‚Üí Simplify the brief
  - ‚Üí Focus on implications (not just findings)
  - ‚Üí Clarify decision needed

- **Decision framework missing?**
  - ‚Üí Articulate what decision(s) are needed
  - ‚Üí Outline strategic options
  - ‚Üí Suggest criteria for deciding

---

## What This Phase DOES Include

‚úÖ Compelling strategic narrative
‚úÖ Story arc (current ‚Üí challenge ‚Üí analysis ‚Üí insight ‚Üí choice)
‚úÖ Customized stakeholder narratives
‚úÖ Key messaging framework
‚úÖ Supporting evidence and examples
‚úÖ Decision framework outlined
‚úÖ Executive communication prepared
‚úÖ Alternative perspectives addressed

---

## What This Phase DOES NOT Include

‚ùå Final recommendations (that's DECIDE)
‚ùå Implementation planning (that's ACT)
‚ùå Change management strategy (that's ACT)
‚ùå Polished presentations (ready to use, not pretty)
‚ùå Complete stakeholder communication plan

---

## Common Blockers & How to Resolve

| Blocker | Signal | Resolution |
|---------|--------|-----------|
| **Narrative feels data-heavy** | "Too many numbers" | Weave evidence into story; don't append analysis |
| **No emotional resonance** | "It's interesting but who cares?" | Add examples, customer stories, real impact |
| **Too many messages** | "We have 15 key messages" | Ruthlessly consolidate; focus on 3-5 core |
| **Stakeholders misaligned** | "Different groups interpret differently" | Create customized narratives for each |
| **Decision unclear** | "What are we actually deciding?" | Articulate explicitly; outline options |
| **Overcomplicated** | "Too hard to explain" | Simplify story arc; focus on essentials |

---

## Post-Completion Actions

Once this checklist passes:

1. **Create Strategic Narrative Document**
   - Full story arc documented
   - Evidence woven throughout
   - Implications emphasized
   - Decision points clear

2. **Prepare Executive Summary**
   - 2-3 page brief
   - Situation, findings, implications, decision
   - Presentation-ready
   - Speaker notes included

3. **Compile Stakeholder Narratives**
   - Each key stakeholder group has version
   - Core message consistent
   - Customization relevant
   - All versions coordinated

4. **Create Persona Handoff**
   - Use `persona-handoff-template.md`
   - Narrative summary
   - Decision framework outlined
   - Stakeholder perspectives documented
   - Execution considerations noted

5. **Prepare for Decision Phase**
   - Share narrative documents
   - Share message framework
   - Prepare presentation materials
   - Confirm Advisor ready for DECIDE

6. **Hand off to Strategic Advisor**
   - Share all narrative materials
   - Confirm Advisor ready to facilitate decisions
   - Load DECIDE phase files

7. **Archive STORY Materials**
   - Save all narratives
   - Document stakeholder feedback
   - Reference for future phases

---

## Notes & Observations

Use this space to capture phase-specific insights:

- **What was the most compelling part of the story?**

- **Which stakeholder group resonated most?**

- **What concerns did we hear?**

- **For future engagements:**

---

## Sign-Off

**Date Completed:** __________________
